Current Commentary

Abolish Oppressive Levies and Supervise Tax Administration 38

The abolition of excessive and miscellaneous taxes has long been a unanimous call from the people. The current fiscal conference took this as one of its four major topics. After deliberation, it was decided that from July of the 23rd year of the Republic of China until the end of December, local authorities should, based on their circumstances, abolish them one by one, sooner or later, to alleviate the suffering of the people. According to the years of disturbance caused by harsh taxes, much is due to the corruption of collection methods, while the actual revenue for the public is not much. If good taxes can be organized, burdens shared equally, embezzlement eliminated, and expenditures adjusted, then the abolition of harsh taxes will not be very difficult. However, the current conference still believes that during the period when provinces and cities are preparing for local autonomy, there are many undertakings that should be carried out, and the reliance on miscellaneous taxes for funding is countless. If proper planning is not done and only the reduction or exemption of various taxes is ordered, it may be a case of "throwing out the baby with the bathwater." Therefore, it was carefully decided that from the next year, the stamp tax, a central government revenue item, will be prioritized as a subsidy for local areas, and the entire tobacco and alcohol license tax will be assigned to local areas for collection. The judicial expenditure item, which was originally paid by local areas, will also be borne by the central government once the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Judicial Administration have a solution. Such painstaking effort and meticulous consideration are all about considering both the legal and practical aspects, and seeking a way to [mutually support both domestic and international affairs].

Now, according to repeated reports from the Ministry of Finance's Local Tax Consolidation Committee, the tobacco and alcohol license tax, which the central government uses to compensate local areas, was allocated to local areas on July 1st. With the power of local administrative authority as a strong driving force, tax revenues have generally increased. The stamp tax item has also been sold by post offices since November. As long as the assessment and collection are appropriate, tax revenues will definitely be considerable. With such ample compensation for all the harsh taxes, they should no longer exist. If local areas still delay and wait and see, or make excuses to shirk responsibility, they will not only be defying the central government's laws and regulations, but also failing the expectations of our people. With our own vital interests at stake, how can we not promptly correct them and allow them to continue to be exploited?

Fortunately, the current fiscal conference also considered this and made a resolution to establish provincial and municipal tax supervision committees. According to the information, except for provinces and cities that have already established councils, the Ministry of Finance will select five to seven impartial individuals with good reputations in the province or city and submit their names to the Executive Yuan for appointment as committee members. The committee's powers are fivefold: (1) Investigate the harsh and miscellaneous taxes and collection situation within the territory. (2) Study methods for consolidating taxes within the territory. (3) Report to the provincial and municipal governments and finance bureaus on the tax situation and consolidation methods within the territory. (4) Report to the Control Yuan on illegal taxes and the illegal behavior of tax agency personnel within the territory. The intention is to give the people the opportunity to participate in the consolidation of local finances and to respect the people's right to supervise local finances.

Now, the deadline for abolishing harsh taxes at the end of last year is less than a month away. It has been repeatedly reported that local areas have been able to uphold the central government's intentions, sympathize with the people's suffering, and implement abolition. However, there may still be cases of those who outwardly comply but inwardly resist. Our country is vast, transportation is difficult, and local situations are extremely isolated. Often, the people's grievances are not conveyed to the higher authorities, and the people's opinions cannot be expressed. General corrupt officials can then deceive the central government and engage in private gain and corruption. In view of this, the Ministry of Finance has already submitted to the Executive Yuan for approval a decision to organize provincial and municipal tax supervision committees as previously agreed. The selection of committee members has also been extensively consulted. Those who are selected by the government to serve as committee members should be keenly aware of the importance of their mission and should not abandon their responsibilities, make excuses to shirk responsibility, or be intimidated by violence and remain silent. As for the local authorities, they should stimulate their conscience and cooperate with each other to consolidate local finances and relieve the people's suffering. Now is the time. Now is the time.

Progress of the American Recovery 39

(New York) The American Bankers Association's monthly report today generally stated that the recovery movement has made progress in recent weeks. Roosevelt Swims and Discusses National Affairs 40

Preparing for Next Congressional Session

Warm Springs, USA A swimming pool here today had four people wearing swimsuits, discussing matters of great importance to the future of the United States. After the talk, all four jumped into the pool and each drank a glass of fruit juice. These four people were President Roosevelt, Federal Relief Administrator Hopkins, the newly appointed Director of the Recovery Administration Lee Geber, and Undersecretary of Agriculture and key member of the [Brain Trust] Tugwell. They discussed the recovery bills that the government should propose in the next Congress and closer coordination between the New Deal departments. It is reported that a decision has been made regarding government proposals, but the nature of this decision has not yet been revealed. (National Telegraph, 1st)

(Washington) President Roosevelt is currently touring the southern states and will soon return to Washington. However, he will face a difficult problem to be resolved by the President. According to Federal Relief Administrator Hopkins, he advocates requesting approximately 900 million yuan from Congress to completely solve the unemployment and relief problem. However, some people in the Relief Administration advocate reducing federal government expenses and hope to promote economic recovery so that private enterprises can hire more workers. Then, the unemployment and relief problem will be solved easily. Which of the two will prevail will depend on the President's decision. (Havas dispatch, 1st)

Borah Advocates Reorganizing the Republican Party 41

Deeply in Accordance with the Intentions of the Youth Faction

Republican Progressive Senator Borah today demanded that the party be completely reorganized. Borah said that the members of the Republican National Committee must be changed, and he indicated that the chairman of the Executive Committee, Fulan Que, and the Republican leader of the House of Representatives, Snell, must both be removed from their positions. Borah's demands are deeply in accordance with the views of the party's youth faction. The youth leaders believe that Fulan Que's recent speech, which stated that the Republican Party should follow the policies set by former President Hoover and remain conservative, because the American people will soon abandon President Roosevelt's policies and demand a return to the old situation, is the reason for their repeated failures over the past two years. Moreover, Fulan Que has never been enthusiastic about welcoming younger party members, which has also caused various dissatisfactions. Some political observers believe that the Democratic and Republican parties in American politics will both disappear and be replaced by two new parties, Liberal and Conservative. Over the past two years, party lines have often been blurred. The progressive faction of the Republican Party has long become Democrats, and the conservative faction of the Democratic Party has long become Republicans. This election also took supporting or opposing the New Deal as the point of contention, rather than party affiliation. (National Telegraph, 1st)

Dutch East Indies Rubber Export Regulations 42

Batavia The government of the Dutch East Indies today promulgated new regulations on the export of rubber planted by Europeans and the Ten Races. From the 15th of this month, only officially recognized plantation owners or rubber merchants may store more than 100 kilograms of rubber. The number stored by other Ten Races producers may not exceed twice the number produced by their rubber plantations each month. The total amount stored by officially recognized rubber exporters must not exceed one-eighth of the regional export limit. The rubber stored by resellers may not be stored for more than two weeks. (Reuters dispatch, 1st)

International Wheat Conference 43

Meeting in London Again at the End of the Month

Budapest The representatives of the world's four major wheat exporting countries, who recently attended the International Wheat Conference here, will gather in London at the end of this month to reach a compromise. The Wheat Advisory Committee today issued a public statement explaining the reasons why a resolution could not be reached at the international conference. It is said that a resolution had to be delayed until the major wheat exporting countries reached a compromise. According to news from Paris, the cabinet has passed a bill that the French government will purchase excess wheat reserves from 1933 to 1934, at a cost of more than 33 million pounds. According to a Reuters dispatch from Washington, Canadian Wheat Board Chairman Macfarlane is currently consulting with the US Department of Agriculture on transporting 15 million or 20 million bushels of frost-damaged wheat into the US to be used as livestock feed. It is reported that the US Treasury Department will allow this wheat to enter the country, levying a special tax of 10 percent on the value instead of the usual tax of 42 cents per bushel. (Reuters dispatch, 1st)

US and Britain Refuse to Negotiate Directly with the Puppet State 45

British Naval, Land, and Air Forces Conduct Exercises in Singapore

Twenty-one Warships Stationed in China Also Participate

Newly Built Naval Port Tests Defenses for the First Time

(Washington) The US government today instructed Ambassador Grew in Japan that the US refuses to negotiate directly with the [Manchukuo] government regarding the oil monopoly issue. The State Department also instructed Grew to lodge a serious protest with the Japanese government against the [Manchukuo] oil monopoly, because this kind of measure violates the Four-Power Treaty's responsibility to maintain the Open Door policy. Grew has considerable freedom regarding protest procedures, but the original position of the United States must be adhered to. It is understood that Britain has also refused to recognize [Manchukuo] as an independent government and that all protests must be submitted directly to it. (National Telegraph, 1st)

Singapore The British Navy is concentrating here today to participate in joint naval, land, and air force exercises to test the strength of Singapore's defenses. The exercise will begin on the 12th of this month. Warships stationed in China have also arrived here to prepare for the exercise. On Sunday, the aircraft carrier Eagle, the destroyer Vittoren, and the Wayke arrived here to anchor, marking the first use of the newly built naval port. There will be twenty-one warships coming from China, and the other land and air forces will also participate in full force. It is said that the naval commander intends to test what would happen if Singapore were attacked and the defense force only had torpedo boats and airplanes. The cause of this exercise is said to be the influence of recent developments in the Pacific. The near failure of the London Naval Talks, Japan's desire to abolish the existing naval treaty, and the increasingly serious commercial competition between Britain and Japan have completely broken the old British-Japanese alliance. All of this is the cause of this exercise. Singapore is the most important link between the Suez Canal and Australia. Australia is very anxious about defense. Former Prime Minister Hughes recently said, "Australia is the most vulnerable country in the world. It is only a stone's throw away from a certain Asian country, so Australia must be prepared, because Britain is no longer the master of the sea, and Japan is no longer our ally." (National News Agency dispatch, 2nd)

Naval Negotiations Show Signs of Compromise Again 46

After the Expiration of the Washington Treaty

A New Treaty Will Be Signed, Valid for Ten Years

(London) The naval talks are now showing new hope that a new treaty can be signed after the expiration of the Washington Treaty, with a term of ten years. According to the new treaty, all signatories must first announce their naval programs for the first five years of the treaty. What will happen in the latter five years has not yet been decided, but if the signatories are not willing to compete in building warships at that time, a meeting may be held to decide the naval programs of the countries in the latter five years of the treaty. Well-informed sources now believe that Japan will definitely agree to this treaty. However, it is said that Japan now keenly wants to know Britain's more detailed needs under this treaty.

When Japanese chief delegate Yamamoto went to the British Admiralty yesterday, the department provided him with a lot of information. However, British and Japanese naval experts still seem to need to continue talking. The Japanese delegation will continue to exchange views with the Tokyo government before it can announce its practical decision.

US chief delegate Davis has not yet expressed his attitude towards the proposed new treaty, but has telegraphed his government for instructions. It is said that the new treaty will not mention ratios. However, Japan will reveal the [implied] or non-numerical ratios, which can be interpreted as allowing Japan a naval position superior to the current 5:5:3 ratio.

The British representatives are now making every effort to prevent the complete failure of the naval talks. The British representatives believe that if the Japanese delegation leaves London without reaching an understanding, all hope will be lost. (Reuters dispatch, 2nd)

The opportunity for better understanding and closer cooperation between the people of Britain and the United States has never been greater or more numerous than it is today. The American saying "the proposer is the President, the decision-maker is Congress" is no longer accurate. It must be known that no US President has ever increased his majority in the mid-term elections. Only President Roosevelt has done so. If Britain reaches an understanding with President Roosevelt, it is tantamount to establishing a lasting understanding with the United States. President Roosevelt will never submit to Congress any bill that he is not sure Congress will agree to. If Britain and the United States agree on a solution to any diplomatic problem, no coalition of forces can resist it. Wall Street no longer commands Washington. Dollar diplomacy is over. The United States now has a brand new and reliable foundation for confidential diplomacy. In view of the recent remarks by British Privy Councilor Baldwin and South African Minister of Justice Smuts regarding the direction of British policy, the opinions expressed by US Ambassador Bingham today are considered to have special significance. Among them, the military budget has exceeded 1 billion yuan, and even the budgets of the Ministry of Interior and the Ministry of Agriculture and Forestry have been reduced. Where Britain's True Intentions Lie 53

(London) Yesterday, Yamamoto, the chief Japanese specialist, presented his personal views to Admiral Chatfield, the British Chief of Naval Staff. His intentions were nothing more than two main points: first, technical experts should meet together to discuss the numbers so that they can easily understand each other; second, British naval leaders should clearly understand that the total tonnage system advocated by Japan is far less alarming than extending the existing treaty's restrictions. Yamamoto's remarks were mostly directed at British naval circles. Naval Admiral Keyes, a famous veteran of the British Navy, has repeatedly declared in recent months that if the London Naval Treaty is continued, it would be an unforgivable betrayal of national interests. Other responsible people in naval circles have also said that the 5:5:3 ratio stipulated in the Washington Treaty is purely for the convenience of American naval strategy. In addition, British Admiralty spokesman Beaverbrook recently published an article in the [Fortnightly Review] stating that the relative strength and absolute strength of the British Navy have been greatly weakened compared to before it was restricted by the treaty. The superior position of the British Navy in 1921-22 has now become a thing of the past and is no longer to be mourned. The so-called equality between the British and American navies is only equality on paper. If you don't believe it, you can compare warships of all classes. The United States, if necessary, must maintain its Open Door policy in the Far East, and fifteen battleships of 35,000 tons each are sufficient. Conversely, based on the experience of the Great War, Britain must have two main fleets, one to be ready to be dispatched to any place where an emergency occurs, and the other to guard the European seas. Therefore, Britain must have at least 20 battleships. As for the tonnage of battleships, it is not a big problem to reduce it to a limit of 25,000 tons. This is one. As for cruisers, the same is true. The main purpose of American cruisers is to cross the Pacific Ocean to the Far East, while the purpose of British cruisers is to protect merchant ships that supply Britain. The London Treaty stipulates that Britain has 50 cruisers, which is too few, and the tonnage of each cruiser is limited to 10,000 tons, which is too high. This is two. Finally, in terms of destroyers and submarines, the restrictions of the current treaty are also impractical. What's more, France and Italy did not sign the London Treaty and are not subject to its restrictions. This is three. For this reason, if Britain acknowledges Japan's principle of naval total tonnage equality, its harm is not as great as maintaining the current restrictions. Therefore, Britain has the possibility of accepting Japan's demands after weighing the gains and losses. In particular, well-informed sources in Britain believe that Japan's finances are exhausted. Even if it is given naval equality, it cannot actually achieve equality with Britain and the United States. Therefore, it is more than willing to accept Japan's demands. However, the final decision on Britain's attitude belongs to the government authorities. At present, any actions that would damage American sympathy for Britain are particularly unacceptable to public opinion. Therefore, even if Britain accepts Japan's demands, it cannot but have some concerns. However, since the British naval community has a tendency to oppose the current naval treaty, coupled with Japan's diplomatic activities, it may eventually become a decision over time, which is also to be expected. (Havas dispatch, 1st)

Severe Cold and Heavy Snow in Northern United States 54

Detroit The northern United States, from the Great Lakes to the Pacific coast, is suffering from severe cold, followed by heavy snow. U.S. Naval Status 55

(Washington) Secretary of the Navy Swanson, in his annual report for 1934 released today, reiterated that the United States is determined to build warships to the limits permitted by naval treaties. At the same time, he stated that if other countries are willing to reduce their naval power, the United States is also willing to reduce accordingly. He added that he firmly believes that to protect the national interests at risk, the U.S. Navy should be no less capable than that of any other country. Swanson continued that the most important task of the Navy Department this year was to enact laws, stipulate naval strength, and authorize the construction of warships and aircraft, so that the Navy can reach the strength stipulated by the treaty and replace old ships that have exceeded their service life. This involves the work of seventy warships, which is currently underway. When this project is completed within the next thirty months, the strength of the U.S. Navy will still be short of approximately seventy-eight warships compared to the limits set by the treaty, and it is hoped that Congress will approve the necessary funds annually to replace old ships. Swanson strongly advocated increasing the number of naval officers and soldiers, saying that the number of soldiers required to be recruited next year is 86,815, while the Navy's funding is only sufficient to support 81,500. A navy built to the treaty limits would require at least 7,000 naval officers, so the number of officers should be increased as soon as possible. Swanson then mentioned aviation affairs, saying that he firmly believes that the U.S. Naval Aviation Corps under the current system is no less powerful than that of any other country, and that any hasty changes, such as organizing unified aviation affairs, would be a big mistake. Swanson's report did not touch on the London Naval Conference issue. (2nd Reuters dispatch)

Acceleration of Japan-Manchukuo Transportation 56

(Dalian) Recently, land and air parties have repeatedly planned to increase the speed of Japan-Manchukuo transportation. Therefore, Osaka Shosen Kaisha is also secretly contacting the connecting ship project to accelerate it and is starting to establish its specific plan. It is heard that the fundamental conditions of the plan are as follows: 1. The average speed of ships traveling between Japan and Manchukuo should be 22 to 23 knots, and two such ships should be built. 2. They should operate exclusively between Dalian, Moji, and Kobe, or be used exclusively between Dalian and Moji. 3. If they operate as dedicated ships between Moji and Dalian, they must travel daily, and the speed should be reduced by 15 hours compared to the current time. 4. When traveling between Dalian, Moji, and Kobe, the time should be shortened by 45 hours compared to the current time. 5. If shipbuilding starts as early as next spring, navigation can be started in 1936. (2nd Japanese Joint dispatch)

Japan-France Gold Franc Case 57

(Paris) In 1912, the city of Tokyo, Japan, raised a foreign debt of 9.17 million francs, of which 4 million pounds were raised in France. Later, due to the depreciation of paper currency after the war, the city of Tokyo refused to repay in gold francs, leading to a long-standing dispute between the two parties. French bondholders then organized a Gold Loan Committee to handle the matter. Congressman Gerin submitted a written question to the Minister of Foreign Affairs regarding this matter, and Foreign Minister Laval also responded in writing. His reply was published in the government gazette today, stating that, according to a report from the French Embassy in Japan, the foreign debt borrowed by the city of Tokyo in 1912 was used entirely for two purposes: (1) purchasing the materials and equipment of the Tokyo Electric Tramway Company, and (2) expanding the facilities to supply electricity within the city of Tokyo. Since the beginning of the dispute between French bondholders and the Tokyo city government, the French Embassy in Japan has continuously protested to the Japanese government and the Tokyo city government, so that French bondholders can be satisfied, but negotiations have not yet yielded results. The Foreign Minister also stated that if French bondholders agree to be repaid in paper francs, there is no reason to file any lawsuits against the Tokyo city government. The Foreign Minister continued that French bondholders have the right to demand that the city of Tokyo execute the judgment of the French court, and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs has always paid attention to this. In addition, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs has instructed the embassy in Japan to pay attention at all times and to assert France's legitimate demands whenever there is an opportunity. (2nd Havas dispatch)

Italy Invents New Method for Mosquito Extermination 58

Rome: Italy has invented a new method for mosquito extermination. The method involves using the oil residue from engines and, through a special chemical method, creating a medicine that is poured into water storage areas in malaria-prone regions, thus eliminating mosquitoes. Traditionally, kerosene has been used for mosquito extermination, which is very expensive. The new method is much cheaper. Prime Minister Mussolini is very interested in this invention and has issued a special decree to commend the inventor and give a generous reward. This method has been tested during the improvement of the Pontine Marshes, and the results have proven to be irresistibly effective in destroying mosquitoes and larvae. The authorities have now drafted a large-scale mosquito extermination plan, which will be implemented starting in March next year. (2nd Havas)

Bucharest: Foreign Minister Titulescu discussed various international issues with the French authorities in Paris a few days ago, and has now completed the discussions. He returned to the country today and reported to the King on the recent international situation. He will stay in the capital for three days and then go to Geneva to participate in the extraordinary meeting of the Executive Council of the League of Nations. When Titulescu arrived here, he issued a statement saying, [The authorities of various European countries, regardless of each other, all hold a firm desire to maintain peace. This is what I have gained and can sincerely declare.] He also said that he was very satisfied with the results of his talks in Geneva and Paris, and he will go to Geneva at the beginning of next week to do his best to protect Yugoslavia's interests, which is no different from defending Romania's interests. Today, the first Soviet ambassador to Romania presented his credentials to the King, and Mr. Xi also participated in the ceremony. It is said that Russia and Romania have severed diplomatic relations for sixteen years, and have only recently restored them. (1st Havas dispatch)

French-German Short-Term Trade Agreement 67

(Paris) The new French-German trade agreement was signed here yesterday afternoon. Its content is nothing more than extending the old trade agreement concluded in July for three months. According to an official explanation, as the Saar plebiscite is about to be held, both parties are only willing to conclude a short-term agreement. It is reported that the trade representatives of the two countries will still meet in order to establish a final agreement based on a broader basis, but this will still be carried out after the Saar issue is resolved. (1st National dispatch)

(Paris) A new commercial agreement between France and Germany was agreed upon last night and formally signed this afternoon. Its validity period is only three months. According to well-informed sources, the reason why this time limit is so short is nothing more than that important events will soon occur that will be sufficient to change the status quo. As for the issue of repayment of Germany's debt of about 60 million francs, the two parties have reached an agreement, and they are now studying a repayment plan. The content is to collect all French claims before August 1 of this year, and clear them through bank procedures. Furthermore, the agreement on import quotas was not declared abolished today, so it will be automatically extended. (1st Havas dispatch)

They stopped work on the 1st. Approximately 3,000 men and women in these two factories have stopped working and are unemployed. (2nd Special dispatch)

England, America, and Japan Reopen Naval Reduction Negotiations 73

Extreme Opposition Between America and Japan

England Mediates

The Naval Disarmament Preparatory Conference, which had been suspended for three months, reopened at 10:30 AM on October 23rd at the British Prime Minister's residence on Downing Street. The first meeting involved British representatives MacDonald, Foreign Secretary Simon, Navy Minister Monsell, and several others, along with Japanese representatives Tsuneo Matsudaira, Naval Representative Isoroku Yamamoto, and two others, exchanging opinions. The content of the talks was kept strictly confidential by both sides and not announced to the outside world. Regarding the order of the meeting, it is said that the Japanese representatives merely explained the main points of Japan's disarmament opinions, while the British side posed various questions. The meeting lasted less than two hours. The next day at 10 AM, American representatives Davis and Admiral Standley met with the Japanese representatives at the Claridge's Hotel. The Japanese representatives again explained their position on disarmament. The American side's response, in addition to emphasizing the spirit of peace, expressed the following opinions regarding the talk of equality in armaments:

[It is natural that the security guarantees of all countries should allow them equal rights, which is recognized by the United States. However, countries do not need to have equal armaments, especially if security guarantees are based on a particular country as an opponent, which should not be the security guarantee of other countries. Therefore, it is impossible for a country to feel threatened by other neighboring countries and demand to be allowed to have equal armaments with that country.]

The Japanese side believes that [in any case, there is no other way than to abolish the past ratio system and achieve equality in armaments.] The above is a brief summary and not enough to show the full picture of the London preparatory conference, nor is it sufficient to judge the future outcome. However, the general trend can be seen in general terms. The irreconcilability between the United States and Japan, and the fact that it will become increasingly deadlocked in the future, cannot be concealed. The United States' observations on the Far East are as follows:

(1) Japan has a very active merchant fleet, which is operated very nimbly, and this helps Japan's military preparations from the side. (2) Since the United States has allowed the Philippines to become independent, it is even more of a guarantee that it will not build military fortresses in the Far East. Japan should be very relieved about this and should no longer say that it is insecure about its national defense.

(3) Japan has obtained [Manchuria's] resources, which has greatly increased its wartime capabilities, and its security should also increase accordingly.

(4) Japan is not like the United States, which is located between two major oceans and needs a stronger navy to protect freedom of navigation at sea.

However, what Japan is concerned about is the rapid development of air power, especially the significant progress in heavy bombers. In 1922, the maximum range of an aircraft was no more than 300 miles, but now it has extended to over 2,000 miles. The action radius of battleships at that time was only 2,500 miles, but recently, due to the development of heavy oil engines and other various improvements, the mobility of battleships can extend to more than 3,000 miles. After 1936, after many new ships are built, a 3,500-mile action radius will be concretely realized. In that case, its geographical value will naturally decline a lot. Therefore, Japan will not easily let go of its claim for [equality in armaments]. The United States also believes that the Washington and London treaties are the foundation of peace in the Pacific and even the world. If this foundation is abandoned, a new treaty will inevitably be even more difficult to establish, and there will be even more difficulties in the future.

England also has its fixed position, which is to be the world's dominant naval power. It does not need large ships and cannons, but only wants to have many powerful cruisers. This is tacitly approved by Japan, but difficult for the United States to tolerate. However, England has always been skilled in diplomacy. Since there is irreconcilability between the United States and Japan, it does not need to immediately raise objections, so as not to create a three-way confrontation and cause the overall situation to collapse and become irreparable. Therefore, England wants to act as a mediator to bring the United States' suggestion of maintaining the original ratio and further reducing armaments by 20 percent closer to Japan's claim for [equality in armaments]. However, we see that in the past history of the Geneva Disarmament Conference, the countries involved were unwilling to give up their own interests, such as England's proposal to expand cruisers, which it would not easily concede. The preparatory talks now underway are certainly not as serious as a formal conference, but they can indeed test how future changes will occur. It is a very accurate barometer. Therefore, from the current situation, it is not yet optimistic. (October 25th in London)

Page 9

Inspection Notes from the Northwest by Our Special Correspondent, Geng Ya 74

Suddenly Heard Bandit Alarm at Hong Liu Yuan

On the morning of the 7th, we departed from Bai Dunzi. After leaving the village for three or four li, sand dunes stretched out on both sides, forming a small yellow sandy basin, thinly covered with black and white gravel, resembling Xiaogan sesame candy. Beyond this, salt flats stretched as far as the eye could see, with dry reeds growing on them, shaped like bamboo, two or three feet high, several zhang apart, interspersed with clumps of camel thorn, all of which camels love to eat. After more than ten li, chaotic mountains rose and fell, though not high, they blocked the line of sight. Suddenly, we came to open ground, overlooking the distant mountains, which were lush and beautiful, only revealing their winding and rugged peaks below the horizon. As if there was a vast miasma in front, the shadows of the peaks were reflected in it, undulating with the wind, wonderfully strange. This kind of Gobi miasma is also called malarial air. Some say that if people accidentally touch it, it will inevitably lead to malaria and other diseases, but it is not easy to touch it. But know that this air is visible from a distance, but there is nothing up close. If one sees miasma elsewhere, others see it in oneself, also in the miasma. It is not easy for people to touch it, but they also touch it from time to time, especially without realizing it. As for whether those who touch it get sick or not, it is related to their original health, and it cannot be concluded that it is only the rampages of miasma.

We met a sick youth, about eighteen or nineteen years old, with hair three or four inches long, unkempt like a clump of grass, lips parched and unable to form words, staggering and shouting, "Eight days without food, eight days without food." We gave him steamed buns, which he swallowed hastily and choked on. Observing his clothing and behavior, he must have received three years of military training, even if he did not graduate from middle or primary school. At that time, the cold wind was blowing, and his whole body was shivering. Mr. Su could not bear it and gave him his fur coat. When asked who he was and why he was so miserable, he did not answer. Mr. Su suspected that something was wrong and asked loudly again, "If you don't tell the truth, I won't give you the coat." He still murmured to himself, "Eight days without food." The reporter then pointed to his ear, intending to ask if he was deaf. He shook his head and replied, "Hungry and deaf, hungry and deaf." Unable to get any information, we each went our own way. The camel driver questioned Mr. Su, "Xingxing Gorge is very cold. Why did you give away the old sheepskin coat?" Mr. Su replied, "I have personally experienced the suffering of cold and hunger. Mr. Su walked through Wuyuan and got lost while rushing. He was frozen and hungry by the Yellow River for a whole day and night. Besides, this thing was also given to me by someone. He is sick, so I am willing to give it to him." A certain Western philosopher once had the theory that "human beings have no sympathy." Now, looking at the matter of giving away the coat to a stranger, it can be seen that this is not entirely true.

Forty li away, in a sandy valley, there were several circles of stone-built ruins. After another ten li, stone ridges rose and fell like waves, mostly green, looking like grass from a distance, interspersed with snow-white gravel, like a waterfall. Red willow and green artemisia, clumps every few steps, the autumn scenery of the desert is really no less beautiful than the red maple and green cypress of Jiangnan. Then we arrived at Hong Liu Yuan for the night, a total of seventy li. As soon as we set up our tents, unexpected guests came, telling us that four bandits had been discovered near Xingxing Gorge. It was said that there were still three people in the mountains, and the bandits were carrying a rifle and a pistol each. They had been robbing for three days, and about four groups of merchants had been robbed, seven people had been killed, and the losses included more than thirty camels, more than ten bolts of cloth, and dozens of taels of gold. Xingxing Gorge is still three stations away from here. After discussion, it was decided that the reporter should draft a letter to request the Anxi Ma Regiment Leader to send a team to escort us. The letter was sent back overnight by the merchant Aximu, while the rest of the camel team continued to advance to Daquan and wait. In the middle of the night, the dogs barked wildly. The camel driver heard it and suddenly came out of the tent and roared loudly. When asked, he said that it was a wild wolf trying to attack the camel formation. (Camels walk in single file, which is called a camel team. At night, they lie down in a circle or in a row, which is called a camel formation.) Therefore, the camel driver roared to scare it away. In late autumn and early winter, it is the mating season for wild wolves. After one female, there are always several males following, howling all night, which can be heard for several li. Travelers should be very careful when encountering them.

The next morning, we got up to look around. All we could see was horse lotus grass, and not a single red willow. There was a shallow well built of stone, with clear spring water overflowing outside, enough for ten camels to drink at the same time. There were several acres of fertile land, but no one cultivated it. There were more than twenty abandoned houses within a dozen steps, and temples such as the Guandi Temple and the Lao Jun Hall were also dilapidated. Five li outside the village, the mountains surrounded it on all sides. During the Guangxu period of the Qing Dynasty, gold mines were opened in the mountains, and gold miners and shops gathered in Hong Liu Yuan, bustling like a small town. Now, there are only two postmen, one going back and forth to send mail, and the other guarding the dilapidated walls and ruins, resting and working in shifts, like the stars that never meet. Nothing is more desolate in the world. Investigating the reasons for the destruction of the postal stations on the Gansu-Xinjiang road, it was due to the disturbances of Wu Tingzhang and Ma Zhongying since the eighteenth year of the Republic of China. Large groups of troops entered Xinjiang, trampling back and forth, and the residents fled one after another. The houses were all demolished to be used as fuel. (Especially Ma Zhongying, during his second trip to Xinjiang in the twenty-second year, did his best to destroy the postal stations he passed, in order to show his determination to succeed and never return.) As a result, the once prosperous villages and towns often turned into desolate ruins. This is not only the case for Hong Liu Yuan and other stations, but also what we saw along the way after entering Xinjiang. Moreover, from Bai Dunzi in the east to Ma Lianjing in the west, the four stations in Gansu are all important border areas. During the Qing Dynasty, each station had a foreign commissioner stationed with ten soldiers. In the early years of the Republic of China, the Anxi Security Team stationed one soldier. Now, even this one soldier is long gone. No wonder four or five bandits dare to seize the opportunity to rob and plunder.

We set off at ten o'clock. The ridges and peaks undulated and crisscrossed. Although the road was very winding, it was still wide and flat, and cars could pass through it. The mountains were all stone and rock, red, black, blue, and white, clearly visible. After being washed by mountain floods for a long time, the sand and gravel flowed down to form rivers, each presenting colorful borders according to the quality of the mountain, interspersed with artemisia and willow, in neat rows, dazzlingly illuminating, like paving rainbows, which can be quite beautiful. At dusk, we met a postman, with a green square scarf wrapped around his head, wearing a green "postman" jacket, and long leather boots on his feet, dressed quite like a martial arts supporting character in a Peking opera. He was riding a small donkey carrying mail, with nine copper bells hanging on his chest, the donkey walking briskly, and the bells ringing. Asking about the situation ahead, he replied that he had not heard anything. The bandits did not rob the mail, was that true? We stayed overnight at Yaozhan [Xiaoquan], a total of fifty li. There were also no houses in Xiaoquan. Digging sand to get water, two feet deep, the water flowed out immediately, but when the wind rose and the sand flew, it was soon buried. Therefore, those who wanted to give water to the camels often dug it temporarily.

In the middle of the night, a camel team suddenly came from a side road. The camel owner, Han Jinfu, often traded between Hami and Suzhou. This time, he was originally going from Dunhuang to Hami, but he heard about the bandit alarm on the way, so he detoured here to join forces. However, he had already detoured five hundred and several tens of li. Han said that there were indeed seven bandits, four of whom were prisoners from Dunhuang Prison who had recently escaped from prison and joined forces to rob. Although there had been several cases of travelers being robbed, Anxi and Hami both had large armies stationed there, and these bandits would be difficult to stay for long.

The Second Plenary Session of the War Zone Clearance Committee 75

Many Proposals, Meeting Scheduled for Three Days

The Three Current Priorities of the Clearance Work

Beiping Correspondence: The War Zone Clearance Committee was established on the first day of last month. It has been a month. This morning (the 1st) at ten o'clock, the second plenary session was held. Except for Standing Committee member Yin Tong, who remained in Tianjin due to official business and was unable to attend, Standing Committee members Li Zeyi, Zhu Shiqin, Committee members Yin Rugeng, Tao Shangming, Yue Kaixian, Xu Tongxin, and Chief Secretary Wang Bihou all attended. First, Wang Bihou reported on the letters and documents received and the proposals submitted by the committee members over the past month. Then, Yin Rugeng, Tao Shangming, and Yue Kaixian reported in detail on the situations in the Ji-Mi and Luan-Yu districts, and eastern Chahar, respectively. At twelve o'clock, there was a break for lunch. The meeting continued at two o'clock in the afternoon. Due to the large number of proposals from the committee members, the agenda for this plenary session was scheduled for three days. Tomorrow (the 2nd) is a regular weekly holiday. The meeting will continue the day after tomorrow (the 3rd) and will close on the 4th. Therefore, during the meeting time this afternoon (the 1st), the committee members only selected the most important of the proposals to exchange opinions separately, and the meeting adjourned at about five o'clock. According to a committee member's statement to the reporter after the meeting, today's meeting was mainly to exchange opinions on the main issues and did not involve concrete discussions. During the three-day meeting, they planned to negotiate the most important work plan and determine the steps. Because the various clearance tasks in the war zone were related to various relevant agencies, it was necessary to complete the pre-negotiations in order to avoid temporary difficulties. According to his speculation, the work plan could be negotiated at this meeting and then submitted to Chairman Huang of the Political Reorganization Council for approval. Therefore, all issues in the war zone can be expected to be gradually cleared up in the future, and there will be no more delays. It was also learned that there are about three things that are the current priorities of the clearance work: (1) the training of security teams and police in the war zone; (2) the crackdown on Japanese and Korean ronin in the war zone; (3) the prohibition of drugs and gambling in the war zone. The quality of discipline of the security teams and police in the war zone is closely related to public security. In order to make the public security in the war zone increasingly improved, they will be trained or rectified separately. In the past, accidents in the war zone were mostly caused by Japanese and Korean ronin. In order to reduce accidents, effective measures will be taken with the Japanese side to crack down on their activities, so that they can all live in peace. Secondly, to prohibit drugs and gambling, because ordinary local thugs often collude with ronin to set up gambling dens and sell drugs in order to make petty profits. In the Tangshan area, the spread of flower clubs has been particularly widespread recently. If these two things are not prohibited, the harm will be endless. The above three things are the main points of the clearance work plan. The committee members are carefully considering the clearance methods during this meeting in order to achieve twice the result with half the effort and complete all the clearance work in the war zone within the scheduled six months. (1st)

Chiang Sends Personnel to Supervise the Mopping-Up and Rehabilitation in Various Districts 76

The District Inspectors Have Set Out to Work

Nanchang Correspondence: Chairman Chiang previously divided the National Army joining the suppression of bandits into two types: attacking and mopping up. The attacking army was organized into columns, while the mopping-up areas targeted the areas occupied by the Red bandits and the areas where the bandits formed groups and their guerrilla zones. Considering the terrain of each place, they were divided into several districts, each district being responsible for more than one independent brigade, and the time limit was set to clear them up. The current operation is to facilitate the supervision of the mopping-up and the handling of rehabilitation. Each mopping-up district and attacking unit is assigned a group of bandit suppression inspectors, whose inspection and supervision tasks are as follows: (A) For those belonging to the First Department: whether the commanders at all levels are thoroughly carrying out orders, the quality of combat effectiveness of the officers and soldiers, the economic situation, and whether the management is transparent, and whether there are any malpractices in the departments at all levels. (B) For those belonging to the Second Department: (1) the situation of party and government personnel assisting the army; (2) the quality and strength of the local corps; (3) the general situation of the mass organizations; (4) all local rehabilitation matters. The inspectors for the Ganjiang and Gan-Zhe-Wan mopping-up districts have all been appointed and have set out to inspect. (November 27th)

Ji-Mi Special Commissioner's Office Cracks Down on Illegal People's Corps in Yutian 77

Wang Bingxiao Secretly Organized a People's Corps in Yutian

The Special Commissioner's Office Ordered the County Magistrate to Handle It Carefully

Tianjin Correspondence: The incompatibility between the Yutian People's Corps and the Security Supplementary Team is indeed an important issue in the war zone. Recently, Yin Rugeng and Shibayama came to Tianjin together to negotiate with Major General Umezu, Commander of the North China Japanese Garrison, hoping to obtain the Japanese side's understanding, and then the provincial authorities would implement effective handling measures. Li Zeyi also rushed here the day before yesterday to assist in the negotiations. The Japanese side believes that this matter is not only related to the North China Garrison, but must be agreed upon by the Kwantung Army before it can be expressed. It is said that Shibayama left Tianjin for Changchun last night to inquire about the Kwantung Army's opinion on behalf of our side.

The People's Corps occupying Ya Hongqiao is the Wang Jizong Department, about six or seven hundred people. Wang is Wang Bingxiao, who caused trouble in Yutian this spring and opened fire with the Security Team. After his department was resolved in Yanshankou this spring, he fled alone to the pseudo-state. A month ago, he suddenly received Japanese protection and returned to Yutian, claiming to be ordered by a certain party to organize the Joint People's Corps of Ji, Yu, and Bao Counties, and made himself the commander of the corps. He gathered Zhao Jingqi, Liu Zuoren, and more than a dozen others, secretly occupied the People's Corps, confiscated civilian guns, extorted money, and forced supplies. He also abolished the police stations, causing the Security Team stationed in Yutian to fear retaliation. They piled sandbags at the city gate, built trenches, and defended closely, putting Yutian in a state of anxiety. After Wang and others mixed into the police stations in various districts, the Public Security Bureau and County Magistrate Huang Zhongkai received successive reports, and the Ji-Mi Administrative Special Commissioner's Office was ordered to handle it carefully. The county issued the following announcement: [(Omission above) According to reports from the Lujiang Zhuang Branch Police Station Chief Liang Hanqing, etc., bandits are rampant and robberies occur frequently. Our station has now moved to Liuzhuangzi and merged with the newly organized People's Corps of 100 people, including Liu Zuoren, Zhang Jinqing, Tian Yunong, and Li Yanchi, in order to avoid being threatened by them. According to reports from the Second District Branch Bureau Chief Li Chongqi, the People's Corps is arrogant and has become a reality, forcing the villagers to provide soldiers and guns to increase their power. Now, the residents of various villages have fled one after another and are in dire straits. It is true that the branch police station was forced to move, and a leaflet for extortion was found, with the pseudo-corps emblem stamped on the end of the leaflet. These are submitted for investigation. The various things have been submitted to the county. After investigation, it was found that Liu Zuoren, etc., were using false pretenses, illegally organizing, not only disturbing public security, but also causing unexpected incidents. I have consulted with Guo of the Hebei Province War Zone Security Supplementary Team and telegraphed a report on the case. Now I have received a cold telegram from the Hebei Province Ji-Mi District Administrative Inspector's Office, saying, "The true telegram has been received. In addition to reporting the matter to the Provincial Government for verification, you must take cautious methods to handle it together and prevent it from spreading like wildfire, and report the handling situation at any time," etc. After investigation, it was found that Liu Zuoren, etc., had secretly organized a people's corps, disturbed the local area, and even dared to order the police station to move. They also went to various townships to confiscate civilian guns and force supplies, running rampant in the villages and ignoring the law, which is indeed unforgivable. We should strictly crack down on them to warn the failures. In addition to reporting the handling situation by special telegram, we should urgently announce to the residents of the county and others, all to know, and all to live in peace and not to listen to rumors and disturb each other. If there are lawless people who incite trouble, illegally recruit, and send rations, and do evil as bandits, they will surely be punished according to the law and will not be lenient. Be cautious and do not violate this announcement. (November 30th)]

Fujian Inspection Group's Survey of Taiwan 78

丨 A Glimpse of Taiwan's Industry and Transportation 丨

Xiamen Communication: The [Taiwan Industrial Inspection Group] organized by the Fujian Provincial Government, with Chen Ticheng, Director of the Department of Construction, as the head of the group, comprising twenty-two people, departed from Fuzhou on November 13th and arrived in Taiwan on the 14th. Having completed their inspection by the 24th, they embarked on the Guangdong Maru from Keelung on the 25th, returning to Xiamen at 8:00 AM on the 26th. Wang Gupan, Director of the Special Public Security Bureau and concurrently Magistrate of Siming County, along with various agencies and groups, boarded the ship to welcome them. Tsukamoto Takeshi, the Japanese Consul stationed in Xiamen, also boarded the ship to welcome them. The entire group disembarked and stayed at the Tianxian Inn. On the 27th, they toured famous scenic spots in Xiamen and Gulangyu. On the morning of the 28th, the entire group left Xiamen for Jimei, returning to the province via land through Quanzhou and Putian.

At 10:00 AM on the 26th, Lu Ticheng met with visitors and discussed the itinerary, briefly stating that they departed on the 13th, spending two weeks, with a total of twelve days in Taiwan. The results of the inspection were very favorable. The agricultural and industrial areas of western Taiwan were inspected. The Governor-General's Office was extremely courteous and thorough in its hospitality. Personnel from various technical agencies were open and candid, providing meticulous guidance, making the experience very enjoyable. Taiwan's industries, especially agriculture, forestry, and water conservancy, are highly developed. The most abundant industrial product is sugarcane. The Japanese have been governing Taiwan for forty years, and their construction achievements are very significant. There are three reasons for this: ㈠ Sufficient government power; the government has great authority in the colony, making it easier to implement policies and allowing everything to be done freely. ㈡ The Japanese people are very hardworking and persistent; things often fail, but they can try again and again, constantly striving, without abandoning grand plans due to minor setbacks. ㈢ Sufficient capital; investments are often in the millions. The prosperity of the entire island depends on favorable weather, geographical conditions, and human effort. Currently, the investment in Taiwan's power construction is set at 100 million, and rural water conservancy is set at 50 million. The large forests that thrive in western Taiwan today were improved and cultivated over fourteen years. Most of Taiwan's land is publicly owned. For example, in the western part of the island, government-owned forest land accounts for 80%, while private ownership only accounts for 20%. However, in recent years, due to industrial development and overproduction, it is necessary to seek outlets abroad. The nearest market is the Fujian province, which is an excellent market. Due to the economic downturn, overproduction, and tariff issues, countries are making a fuss. The United States has deeply felt this, and Japan will also feel the same way. While in Taiwan, I stated that Chinese politics are not entirely anti-foreign. In my opinion, future construction in this province does not need to imitate others in everything. We should only take their strengths and strive to move forward, so that we can use our unique features to engage in international exchange with foreign countries, to avoid the continuous increase in annual revenue and the constant outflow of national wealth. After returning to the province, I plan to carry out construction plans within our financial means. First, we will gather talent and resources, and then proceed step by step, one by one. Western Fujian is mountainous and suitable for afforestation and production, such as the Fukien fir, which has the widest range of uses. The Japanese have transplanted it in Taiwan with good results, and we should increase support to make it a special product of our province. The plains in eastern Fujian, such as Fuzhou and Xinghua, are suitable for rice cultivation. We plan to improve water conservancy and expand rice paddies. The province's insufficient rice supply is a matter of great concern. Southern Fujian, Quanzhou and Zhangzhou, are abundant in sugarcane and fruits. Because of this, we should revitalize the sugar industry, and so on.

Inspection Schedule: November 14th, arrived in Keelung at 8:00 AM, then took a train to Taipei, staying at the Railway Hotel. In the afternoon, attended a banquet hosted by the Governor-General's Office and visited the Agricultural Specialized Department of Taipei Imperial University, the Central Research Institute, and other places. In the evening, was hosted by the Bank of Taiwan. On the 15th, visited the Central Research Forestry Department, the Commodity Exhibition Hall, the Museum, the Taipei Prefectural Industrial School, the Agricultural and Forestry Training Institute, the Xinzhuang Mandarin Orange Cultivation area, and other places. Around 10:00 PM, departed from Taipei and slept overnight in the train, arriving in Tainan the next morning. Visited the Sugar Industry Experiment Station. In the afternoon, arrived in Kaohsiung, toured the city, and visited the Pineapple Canning Inspection Office. Arrived at Cape Eluanbi in the afternoon, observing the Seedling Propagation Farm, the Forestry Experiment Station, and the Agricultural School along the way, all thoroughly inspected. On the morning of the 19th, at 11:00 AM, took a car to the Wushantou Jianan Great Irrigation Canal. There are artificial waterways and pools here, with irrigation evenly distributed, so that no water or drought disasters occur. Since its construction, agricultural production has increased threefold. For example, rice has increased by 460,000 shi per year, sugar has increased by 2.4 million dan, and total income has increased by more than 20 million yuan. The value of real estate has also increased to 95 million. On the 20th, went to Ali Mountain to visit timber collection, logging operations, and other activities, which are large in scale. On the 21st, went to Pin Yi, Water Society, and other places. On the morning of the 22nd, at 8:00 AM, visited the Sun Moon Lake Power Plant. The power plant has 100,000 kilowatts, supplying electricity to the entire city, costing 100 million yuan. Returned to Taipei at 9:00 PM that night. On the 23rd, visited the Jiaoshan Tea Factory and other places. On the 24th, went to the Colonial Affairs Bureau, the Police Bureau, the Police Officer and Prison Officer Training Center, the Monopoly Bureau, and the Slaughter Bureau for on-site inspections. On the morning of the 25th, departed from Taipei at 8:00 AM, arriving in Keelung at 9:00 AM. At 10:00 AM, boarded the Guangdong Maru. The trip lasted twelve days. Officials from the Taiwan Governor-General's Office, such as Mr. Katayose, guided the visits along the way. Overseas Chinese in various places held Chinese national flags, shouting "Long live the Republic of China!" Their warm welcome was unprecedented. Overseas Chinese federations and Good Neighborliness Associations all prepared grand banquets, demonstrating a 200,000-point enthusiasm for the motherland, which fully expresses the spirit of our Chinese nation.

Taiwan's Geography: In the 16th century, Portugal was the first to trade with our country. After Macau was ceded, Taiwan was discovered. Its English name [Formosa] is actually a Portuguese pronunciation. Our country calls it Taiwan. In 1895, after Japan annexed Taiwan, it still used our country's original name, which has not changed to this day. The area is 18,839 square miles. The population consists of 4,592,500 Taiwanese, 247,000 Japanese, and 808,000 overseas Chinese, totaling over 4.9 million people. The sea route to Xiamen is 100 miles.

Taiwan's Industry: Two years after Japan occupied Taiwan (1897), its imports and exports were valued at 31 million Japanese yen. By 1930, this had increased to 409.7 million Japanese yen. Agriculture is relatively developed, especially rice. The value of exports from Taiwan to Japanese-controlled territories in 1931 is listed below: Minerals: 4,597,000 Japanese yen; Marine products: 13,912,073 Japanese yen; Yellow Plums: 4,158,000 Japanese yen; Straw hats: 3,838,000 Japanese yen; Sugar: 123,832,000 Japanese yen; Rice: 41,067,000 Japanese yen; Tea: 7,363,000 Japanese yen; Camphor: 2,352,000 Japanese yen; Bananas: 8,329,000 Japanese yen. The total exports for that year, including the above, were valued at 220,873,000 Japanese yen. Imports were 145,622,000 Japanese yen.

Taiwan's Transportation: The government-owned railway has increased to 563 miles, and the commercially owned railway has increased to 1,349 miles. Most of the commercial railways were funded by sugar merchants to transport raw materials or for sugar factory exports. The telephone business is completely government-owned. When it opened in 1900, there were only five exchanges and 431 users. Progress has been made over the years. By the winter of 1933, there were 112 exchanges and 15,700 users, with a total income of approximately 2,712,000 Japanese yen. Japanese users account for approximately 71%, and Taiwanese users account for 29%. Long-distance telephones are readily available, and there are almost none without them in cities, towns, and villages. Takao (i.e., Kaohsiung Prefecture), located at the mouth of the sea, is an important port for foreign trade. In 1932, a new telephone bureau valued at 440,000 Japanese yen was completed there. Because the location is in the tropics, air conditioning is specially installed in the building to keep the room temperature below 75 degrees Celsius all day long. Currently, the bureau has 1,200 automatic telephone users, with an ultimate capacity of 4,800 users. The Takao automatic telephone needs to be specially mentioned because the equipment is manufactured locally in Japan, while other places use equipment manufactured in Europe and the United States. As for long-distance telephone calls to Japan proper, they have already been established in April of this year, through government-business cooperation, with a capital of 10 million Japanese yen. In addition to communication between Taiwan and Japan, there are also plans to connect with countries in Europe, America, and Asia. (November 30th)

The Dexinchang Rice Mill in Xishi Town, Sijing, has always been known for its thriving business. His head was severely injured, and he lost consciousness immediately. Workers rushed to rescue him, but his injuries were quite severe. He was hired a boat to Shanghai for treatment at a Shanghai hospital, but just as he left the mill gate, the injured person had already died. Date: From 8:00 AM to 4:00 PM on the 8th of this month; 2. If it rains or is cold, elementary school Boy Scouts who do not have uniforms may not participate; 3. When fundraising, the Disaster Relief Donation Committee will issue symbols and donation receipt books; 4. On the fundraising day, the Education Bureau will order all schools to suspend classes; 5. Fundraising instructions and a distribution area list will be collected from the council by each group before 12:00 PM on the 7th (Friday); 6. Groups that have not registered the number of participants should register with the council before Tuesday of this week; 7. When fundraising, the attitude should be amiable, the dress should be neat, and the meaning and purpose of the donation should be explained in detail. Do not force donations; 8. When fundraising, you should bring a dry food bag or other similar money bag to store the donations; 9. If special circumstances occur on the fundraising day, or you need to receive more receipts, or have any questions, you can contact the Disaster Relief Donation Committee at the Sichuan Road YMCA. The meeting discussed until 5:00 PM, and the number of registered participants has reached more than 2,000. It is also heard that the Disaster Relief Donation Committee sent a letter to the Federation of Trade Unions to convene a meeting within two days to discuss the fundraising methods for factory employees and workers.

Shanghai Money Market Gradually Loosening 96

Yesterday's Foreign Call Loan Rate Dropped to Twenty Cents

The Shanghai market's need for cash has been increasing daily, leading to an unusually tight money market and soaring foreign call loan rates. It is now heard that the outflow of cash has decreased sharply in recent days, resulting in a gradual easing of the money market. In the money market yesterday morning, the foreign call loan rates opened at 8:30 AM and 12:30 PM, both having dropped to twenty cents, a decrease of fifteen cents compared to yesterday and a decrease of twenty cents compared to the highest point. The discount on head money was twenty-five cents. According to people in the money market, the money market is gradually loosening, and the foreign call loan rate is feared to drop again.

Late Opening of Shanghai-Beiping Through Train Yesterday Afternoon 97

Due to an Obstruction with the Official Special Train at Zhenru Station

Yesterday afternoon at 3:30 PM, an official empty special train on the Beijing-Shanghai Railway, intended to depart from Nanxiang for Shanghai, suddenly stopped a few miles from Zhenru Station. The outer steel wheel axle screw of the locomotive C-16 pulling the train had suddenly loosened, causing it to stop and unable to move forward. Railway staff immediately reported to Zhenru Station, which urgently telegraphed the Shanghai Main Station. At the same time, Nanxiang Station was telegraphed to pay attention to incoming trains from Beijing to Shanghai, to avoid accidents. Upon receiving the news, the Main Station immediately dispatched a repair train to carry out repairs. It was not until 7:05 PM that the repairs were completed, and the train was able to depart for Shanghai. The Shanghai-Beiping through train was delayed for three hours as a result, before it could depart.

Special Survey Record of Domestic Goods Industry 99

(10) Thermos Bottle Industry

Thermos bottles used to be imported goods. The first domestic manufacturer to start this emerging industry was the Guangming Thermos Bottle Factory ten years ago. Afterwards, Lixing, Han Chang, Zhonghua, Samsung, Guangda, Zhenye, Tongchang, Far East, and other factories were established one after another. They flourished and became very popular for a time. At most, there were more than sixty companies. In the past two years, competition has intensified, and the number of factories has been too large, which has led to an oversupply. The industry is declining. Although the amount of foreign goods has decreased, domestic goods have not been selling well, which is a hidden concern for the industry's future. Recently, our reporter interviewed Gan Dounan, the chairman of the Thermos Bottle Trade Association and manager of Lixing Thermos Bottle Factory, Liang Bozhi, manager of Guangming Thermos Bottle Factory, and Wang Zhizhang, manager of Danhua Thermos Bottle Factory, who provided detailed information and gave many suggestions. The following is a record of what was said. There are currently twenty thermos bottle companies, and fourteen of them are members of the trade association. There are two companies that make bottle cores. The annual sales of domestic products are about 2.5 million yuan. The annual business of large factories such as Guangming and Lixing is about 300,000 to 400,000 yuan. Regarding the purchase of raw materials, imported goods such as tinplate and glass sand account for about 40%. Domestic paint can also be used. In terms of labor, many people used to borrow talent from Japan, but recently there have been more and more domestic skilled workers. However, wages are very high, and factories poach workers from each other. The most difficult aspect of production and sales is extending credit to customers. If you are not careful, you will get bad debts. There are no particular difficulties in sales in China. In Hong Kong, due to price relations, they cannot compete with the strong sales of Japanese goods. Currently, the factories that have failed in the industry, such as Lizhong, Guanghua, Shanghai, China, and Yutai, have either stopped working or are in the process of liquidation. The most significant reason for their failure is short capital (small factories in the industry can be established with a capital of 2,000 yuan), and poor technology and shoddy workmanship are also fatal wounds. According to Gan, the thermos bottle industry used to be dominated by foreign goods. Eastern goods had annual sales of 2.7 to 8 million yuan, and Western goods had annual sales of over 1 million yuan. Recently, there have been more and more domestic goods, and Eastern goods are now less than 1 million yuan per year, and Western goods are only 500,000 yuan. It cannot be said that the Chinese people have not worked hard to promote domestic goods, nor can it be said that they have been ineffective. If this industry can cooperate with each other, it will not only have great development but can also be sold overseas. However, there are still many Japanese goods in Tianjin, the Yangtze River area, and the countryside is declining. The purchasing power of the general public is far worse than before. The products of various factories are feeling sluggish, and the price of goods this year has been reduced by 30% compared to last year. According to the opinions of Gan, Liang, and Wang, at present, only the industry can realize, cooperate with each other, and be determined to compete with foreigners. They should not be at odds with each other in China. The first solution is to have excellent products, the second is to have low costs, and the third is to make more patterns. If they can make cheap and good products, why worry about not being able to drive out foreign goods? The leaders of each factory should especially adopt a steady and forward-looking approach, research and create special products, and strive for mass production, maintain industry relations, and strive for overseas markets. Then, the difficult thermos bottle industry may have hope for development. This lies in the thorough awakening and sincere cooperation among the industry. It is vaguely heard that some vendors are ordering brands from Japanese factories, and some small factories are specializing in selling inferior goods, changing their appearance to deceive people, causing domestic manufacturers to suffer. This is something that the industry should have a way to sanction.

After arriving in Shanghai, Mr. Li returned to his residence with his wife and secretary to rest. Regarding the matter of attending the Fifth Plenary Session, according to Mr. Li's conversation with a reporter from the Xin Sheng News Agency yesterday, he had been recuperating from his old illness for quite some time in the countryside, and the supply of medicine and other supplies in the countryside was not as convenient as in Shanghai, and his blood pressure had increased compared to before. When he was examined by a doctor in Jiujiang the day before yesterday, it was 187, so he returned to Shanghai to recuperate. The Fifth Plenary Session is approaching, but he has no preparations for proposals, and it is difficult to determine whether he will attend due to his illness. He had not seen the telegrams of Wang and Jiang, so he did not know about them. He only heard about Wang Liangchou and others going to Hong Kong when he passed through Nanjing the day before yesterday.

Chinese and Foreign Rice Merchants Purchasing a Large Batch of Foreign Rice 104

Totaling More Than 500,000 Dan

It Can Be Shipped to Shanghai Within This Month

This year, China has been plagued by floods and droughts, and the harvest in rural areas has been exhausted. The issue of people's food is gradually becoming serious, and all parties are paying close attention to it. A reporter from Xinxin News Agency specially visited Gu Xinyi, a leader in the local grain business, yesterday. According to him, he discussed the issue of grain in great detail. The details are recorded as follows:

Provinces with Poor Harvests Purchasing from Shanghai According to Mr. Gu, food is one of the most important factors in people's lives, clothing, food, shelter, and transportation. At a time when rural areas are bankrupt and disasters occur frequently, even the provinces that produce the most rice, such as Anhui, are only sufficient to feed themselves. This has led to a serious problem of people's food, and the people themselves feel uneasy. Fortunately, the authorities of various provinces have responded quickly and handled the situation properly, so there is no need to worry. However, according to what I know, the most serious disaster this time is Zhejiang Province. The province's rice production has always been abundant, but this year it is purchasing grain in large quantities from Shanghai for use. The rest of the provinces such as Lu, Ji, and Su have also experienced poor harvests.

Purchasing Foreign Rice to Regulate People's Food The local authorities in Shanghai, in view of the importance of the grain issue, and Shanghai being the hub of transportation for various provinces, specially ordered the Social Affairs Bureau to convene grain merchants to discuss relief measures. It was then decided to purchase foreign rice to regulate people's food. Today, the grain merchants are still able to comply with the price limit set by the Social Affairs Bureau, which is due to the efforts of the local authorities in Shanghai. According to another source, Mr. Gu, in conjunction with major local grain merchants, has ordered 200,000 dan of foreign rice from Annam, and foreign merchants have also ordered as much as 300,000 dan, all of which can be shipped to Shanghai within this month. It is also learned that foreign merchants have already chartered Norwegian ships to transport them to China.
