Order to Improve the Secondary School Normal Department 153

The Ministry of Education issued a general order to the education departments and bureaus of all provinces and cities on the 1st, stating: "Upon investigation, in the past ten years, the number of public and private secondary schools and normal schools has increased sharply, but the quality varies, which has become increasingly apparent. Generally speaking, the equipment of each school is mostly inadequate, the curriculum is chaotic, the teaching methods are outdated, and the education is not fully qualified, resulting in a daily decline in efficiency. The Ministry, in view of this, has successively promulgated standards for secondary schools and normal school curricula and equipment, regulations for teacher certification, and regulations for student joint examinations, in order to improve school curricula and equipment, improve teaching efficiency and student levels, and gradually improve the quality of secondary schools and normal schools. Last year, specialists were again assigned to conduct on-site inspections in various provinces and cities. Based on the reports of the members, orders were issued to comply with the relevant cases. In summary, the reports of the members show that the educational administrative organs of various provinces and cities have, in general, implemented the standards and regulations promulgated by the Ministry, but the situation of chaos and disorder is still common. In severe cases, due to the low level of the past, in order to cope with graduation joint examinations and university entrance examinations, the number of teaching hours has been increased excessively, with some reaching 48 hours per week, violating the principles of learning, damaging the physical and mental health of young people, and causing great harm. In order to correct the accumulated abuses and promote efficiency, the following matters are hereby clarified:

(1) All public and private secondary schools and various normal schools in all provinces and cities should teach in accordance with the prescribed teaching subjects and hours for each grade, and there should be no more differences. For the graduating schools, due to the transition period, the previous teaching has not been sufficient, and it is necessary to prepare for the joint examination, the respective departments and bureaus should determine an appropriate increase in teaching hours, but not exceeding 36 hours per week.

(2) If there are no approved teaching materials for each subject in senior high schools and normal schools, teachers should compile their own teaching materials or select alternative teaching materials in accordance with the curriculum standards of each subject promulgated by the Ministry, and increase or decrease the amount according to the standards.

(3) The equipment fees of all public schools should be purchased in accordance with the equipment standards of the science departments promulgated by the Ministry as soon as possible, and should absolutely not be misappropriated. The board of directors of private schools are responsible for raising funds to enrich the equipment.

(4) All subjects should focus on practical work, such as science and chemistry experiments, biological collection, geographical practice, arithmetic exercises, Chinese reading and writing, and foreign language writing and speaking. Teaching methods should also focus on inspiration and discussion, and should not be purely lectures.

(5) The number of students in each class at all levels of schools shall not exceed the prescribed maximum number. Those who violate this rule will not have their student status reviewed.

The above items shall be implemented uniformly from the second semester of the 23rd year, and the department should conduct strict inspections in accordance with the regulations. The department should immediately comply with the regulations and report accordingly."

Internal Work of the Boy Scout General Association 155

After the Chinese Boy Scout General Association was officially established on November 1, it immediately proceeded actively. The current site (at No. 1 Xinjin Lane, Malu Street) is a Western-style building. Although the scale is not very large, the layout is quite clean and tidy. In addition, the chief secretary of the association, Feng Ti, is effective in his supervision, and the atmosphere is vigorous. The work is particularly intense. Currently, all staff members have been required to wear uniforms, which will be made and altered in the middle of next week. Afterwards, there will be a more neat and solemn appearance. As for the internal work, in addition to setting up four sections in accordance with the general regulations, a legal review committee is also set up to review and revise all previous and current laws and regulations. In order to ensure economic transparency, an economic review committee is also set up. All income and expenditure accounts and purchase receipts and supplies within the association must be reviewed and deemed appropriate before they can be processed. In order to improve work efficiency, the association has stipulated that in addition to the weekly meetings of the office and various departments, each staff member must fill out a work report every day for reference. Each department is assigned one person to be on duty each day, and the chief of the department and above is the general duty officer, who takes turns being on duty in order to deal with official business and maintain internal affairs. Even on weekly holidays, the progress of governance will not be delayed. Recently, in order to understand the personality, knowledge, and governance abilities of each staff member, the chief secretary personally set a test, which all staff members from the department chief to the recorder participated in. The recorder's test papers focused on calligraphy. In addition, the organization and training of boy scouts at all levels throughout the country is currently being drafted. In the future, it will be carried out in an orderly manner, and there will be a reorganization of the future of the Chinese boy scouts.

In addition, after the establishment of the association, two memorial weeks for the Prime Minister were held. In order to connect and build momentum, all directors of the Nanjing Boy Scout Council were ordered to participate. The chief secretary, Feng Ti, gave a speech, with many words of encouragement, and individually met with the directors of the Beijing Municipal Council to learn about the work of the Municipal Council. Therefore, under the close guidance of the General Association, the Beijing Municipal Council will also have a new look. In the future, it is planned to regularly invite directors of the National Council to attend the memorial week speech in rotation. It is heard that Chen Lifu, a director, is scheduled to give a speech next week.

To enable participants to observe the time and fulfill the New Life Movement

Resolution passed by the board of directors and submitted to the municipal party headquarters for review

The Shanghai Municipal Education Association held its second board meeting yesterday. (8) Checking that adhering to the time of meeting is a convention of the New Life Movement, whether it is possible for the association to advocate that all sectors hold a watch alignment ceremony led by the chairman before each meeting, it was resolved: The resolution was passed and submitted to the municipal party headquarters for review. Chih Tze College and Affiliated Middle School Celebrated Their 10th Anniversary Yesterday 160

Yesterday was the 10th anniversary of Chih Tze College and its affiliated middle school. At 10:00 a.m., a celebration ceremony was held in the school's auditorium. At noon, a large-scale dinner party was organized by the student association. More than 1,000 people attended, including faculty, staff, alumni, and male and female students of the school, including He Shimo, He Shimei, He Zuochang, Tang Shichang, Zhang Ke, Zhu Mei, Liu Yunfang, Ren Xianqun, Ni Zheng, Yuan Shuainan, and Pan Jianbo. There was a continuous flow of vehicles on the Shui Dian Road, which was a grand occasion. The details are recorded as follows:

Celebration Ceremony The bell rang ten times, and the school's auditorium was full. He Shimei, the dean of academic affairs, presided over the meeting, Ren Xianqun took the minutes, and Li Niankai served as the master of ceremonies. The ceremony was carried out as usual. First, the president (represented by the dean of academic affairs) reported on the past year, briefly stating that the school was founded to fulfill the last wish of the ancestors, and the establishment of the school was due to anti-communism. Preparations began in the autumn of the 13th year of the Republic of China, and the school was established in the spring of the 14th year. Since then, it has been struggling in difficulties and hardships every day. The new school building was completed, and before June, it was almost completely destroyed due to the January 28th Incident. Before June, the school had completed the repairs before the other schools. Although the equipment was not complete, the basic scale was gradually restored to its original state, which was not easy. The application for registration has been repeatedly frustrated due to various reasons. The ability to have today is entirely due to the unyielding and uncompromising spirit of struggle and the concerted efforts of all faculty, staff, and students. In the future, if there can be a stronger solidarity and a more diligent struggle, the progress of the school will increase day by day, and I hope to encourage everyone. Subsequently, Professor Yao Minghui, Professor Zhang Ke, Professor Wang Xiaowen, representative of the middle school Hao Naiding, and representative of the student association Lu Shidao delivered speeches one after another. The words were sincere and touched the audience. The ceremony ended at 12:30.

Dinner Party The school's student association took this opportunity to connect old and new friends and organized a large-scale dinner party. More than 200 people participated, and Tang Shichang presided over the meeting. It was a very interesting gathering. Zhou Yuchun sang the school song, Ye Mianchang and Yang Junming sang "Catching Cao", He Zuochang and Zhao Juzhi sang "Four Lang Visits His Mother", Mao Yinfang and Yang Qingxin sang "Three Mothers Teach Their Son", and Xia Niuhui Zhen's piano solo and Wu Hanfang's comic show and other recreational activities were wonderful and enjoyable. Each person was given a thick commemorative special issue and a Jiangsu Northern issue.

Little Western Paradise 166

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 5: Putting on a forced smile to welcome, lighting a lamp to illuminate the haggard face; following the trend to learn frivolousness.

Little Ji nodded and smiled, saying, "That's fine too. I'll bring her over tomorrow morning. I could have arranged it for the afternoon, but that would be too long." As he said this, he smiled, and in that smile, there seemed to be a hint of teasing Jia Duocai. Jia Duocai really wanted to see the girl, and since the man had offered, he couldn't refuse, but he felt that this tea boy was not easy to deal with and needed to be wary of him. Little Ji's thoughts were exactly the same. He felt that this wealthy man was different from others and couldn't be easily fooled, so he needed to take a careful approach. At that moment, he sorted out some of the affairs at the hotel and then went to Sister Hu's house. Poor people couldn't afford to light oil lamps, so when it got dark, they would grope their way to the bed and lie down. Even if they couldn't fall asleep immediately, with their head on the pillow, they could think about when they could dig up a cellar of silver under the bed. At this time, Sister Hu was thinking about digging a cellar and was getting a little drowsy when she suddenly heard someone knocking on the door outside. She was startled, wondering if it was the military police coming to arrest criminals. So, even though she heard the knocking, she lay on the bed and didn't dare to make a sound. Later, Little Ji directly called out "Sister Hu," and recognizing the voice, she dared to ask what was the matter. Little Ji had a belly full of plans that couldn't be shouted out loud, so he said, "Since you're asleep, I might as well tell you tomorrow morning. Don't forget to come find me early. There's a one-dollar deal to be made." Sister Hu called out, "Brother Ji, slow down," kneeling on the bed and frantically grabbing for clothes. She said anxiously, "Where did my clothes go? Who took them? Brother Ji, wait a moment, I'll be right there. Oh! These are pants. I thought I was wearing a jacket. No wonder I couldn't put it on. Brother Ji, wait a while, I'll be right there." She spoke softly anxiously, and called out to people loudly, busy for quite a while. (79)

In the Speculative Market 167

— Zhou Xian

One day, I followed a friend to a certain exchange to sightsee.

In the market, the crowd was so dense that I don't have adequate words to describe it. In this crowd, people were constantly pushing and shoving. Alas, those who were pushed and shoved could only use the momentum to support their bodies against the chests and backs of the people in front, behind, or on the sides, causing those people to be pushed and shoved in another direction. Although you want to use the strength in your legs to support your body in a more stable position, it is hopeless. Fortunately, those who squeeze and shove you are also being squeezed and shoved by others, and at the same time, although you are being squeezed and shoved, you can also squeeze and shove others with force. Fortunately, in this place, squeezing and shoving is not a big deal.

Dozens of so-called brokers' agents were jumping, hopping, gesturing, and constantly shouting "[Two jiao]," "[Three jiao]," "[Four jiao]." Originally, the trading market was full of a crazy atmosphere, and these jumping and hopping agents were even more fully expressing a crazy state. But after these agents went crazy once, the market price changed. Then a terrible commotion immediately broke out in the market. You desperately squeeze me, and I desperately shove you. The victors laugh heartily, and the losers stamp their feet and puff out their chests. The original face of humanity is completely revealed here.

I still don't believe that in this atmosphere of pushing and shoving, jumping and hopping, and noisy shouting, one can go from rags to riches, or from riches to rags. But in the market, everyone is anesthetized and goes crazy.

Jianghu Secrets 169

— Rong Yu

[Relying on two lips, without real ability. Speaking flowery words. Deceiving people to get copper coins.] This is the ironclad annotation of "Jianghu Secrets."

A crowd of people surrounded the square. A friend of Jia Quan's demonstrated several sets of fancy boxing, which made the onlookers clap and cheer. Then he took out a plate of plasters, saying they were a secret passed down through generations, and no matter what the injury, one plaster would heal it. The onlookers were moved by his words and were willing to take out money to buy a few to keep for future use. If you ask if the plaster is really effective: that is only [Heaven knows, Earth knows, and I myself know].

A square table, a few long benches, and the fortune-teller sat in a dignified manner. As soon as he saw someone walking by wearing nice clothes, he would say: [Your Excellency has smooth sailing before you, and ten years of good luck to follow;] when he saw someone walking by looking haggard, he would say: [Your Excellency is suffering some troubles now, but you will definitely rise to the top in the future.] People saw that his words were quite accurate, and after a moment's pause, they would invite you in to discuss your life in detail. This is called [Binding Immortal Rope]. Once he releases it, no matter how clever you are, you can't escape the hook. You sit down to examine your fate in detail. He says a lot of words, but they are neither painful nor itchy, neither near nor far. As for how much the price is, it depends on whether your clothes are beautiful or not.

Shaking a string of bells in his hand, shouting [Specially cures all kinds of difficult and complicated diseases]. As soon as a sick person invites him in, he doesn't care what the disease is, he keeps shouting [This disease is dangerous and must be treated quickly]. After a series of frightening words, the sick person becomes anxious. Then he exaggerates his own experience and says [The doctor has the heart to cut his own thigh, I will definitely do my best to treat you; the consultation fee doesn't matter; the medicine is precious, please pay a few tenths first.] You give him the money, and he gives you a few doses of powdered medicine. He doesn't even know what it is, but when he talks about it, it's always precious medicines such as pearl powder and rhinoceros horn. If the disease is cured, he will come back for the money; if it is eaten badly, he will not be responsible. If someone invites him, there is really the possibility of [turning a small disease into a big disease; and ensuring that a big disease leads to the end].

A monk with deep virtue and high practice enters the door to see you. Saying [Someone in your family has been sick recently: someone's speculation is unfavorable] It's as if he saw it with his own eyes, without the slightest error. Then he said [Sickness is caused by vengeful ghosts: financial loss is due to unfavorable years, only if this poor monk performs some rituals of appeasement can it turn bad luck into good luck and turn misfortune into auspiciousness.] The host suspected that a living immortal had descended, and followed his words, worshiping the stars and paying homage to the Dipper, chanting mantras completely. A lot of copper coins were spent, but no effect was seen. However, the maid or driver in the host's house had already gone to the monk to get a kickback.

Geneva Garden (No Littering)

Smoke 170

— Tian Yu

Cigarettes can be considered the only companion for lonely people. When you feel extremely bored and extremely depressed in your heart, and you can't get rid of it, just light a cigarette, lie down on the sofa and smoke it slowly; looking up at the circles and layers of silver-gray smoke, which turn into a dragon colt, winding and twisting upward, lingering on the ceiling, and finally disappearing into the void. How fascinated you should feel! Just now, your depressed and bored mood was unknowingly destroyed without a trace in this fleeting, fleeting process of transformation.

In the past, I could really be said to be a loyal comrade of the [Non-Smoking Society]. At that time, I hated cigarettes like enemies, especially those who smoked, and I held a sense of loathing. Whether it was in a carriage or in a small room, when I smelled the cigarette smell coming from other people's mouths into my nostrils, or the smoke floated to my face, I felt like I had been infected with some kind of evil disease, and I immediately wanted to jump up in anger. Now, I myself have become the person I used to hate and am close to the things I used to hate. Now, almost every day, every hour, I have to smoke a few cigarettes. I have to smoke when I work and study, and I also have to smoke when I rest; otherwise, I will feel uncomfortable. In this way, between me and cigarettes, it is clear that an inextricable bond has been formed.

Why did I suddenly develop such a strong feeling with cigarettes? The reason is very simple, I am very lonely, I need comfort!

Random Words

Miner's Life 171

— Huang Kewei

There was a time when people were dreaming of a golden dream, that is, [Go to Nanyang to dig up a gold mine,] Every year, quite a few people are drawn in to work as miners by this tempting saying, but who has seen a miner dig up a gold mine and return? Some are forever imprisoned on the mine mountain doing hard labor, and some are drained of their blood and sweat, and even their bones are buried in the mine! In recent years, the entire world has fallen into a depression, and that golden South Island is no exception, and the treatment of miners is even more cruel!

It is rare to have a few clear days on the mine mountain, and it is always so gloomy, filled with a humid atmosphere. Every day, early in the morning before the east is bright, a few mine police come blowing whistles, and this sharp sound wakes up the miners lying next to the furnace, and they quickly prop up their tired bodies that have not had enough rest, hastily wipe their faces, eat a few pieces of coarse and dirty noodles, carry a burlap bag on their backs, and carry a pickaxe and magnesium lamp, and hurry out of the house. Under the supervision of the mine police, everyone lined up in a neat row and dragged their heavy steps to work. The mine police looked very fierce, armed all over, with bayonets and wooden-cased guns stuck in their waists, and long guns on their backs. Their eyes were frighteningly fixed on every worker. If they walked slower or chatted with their companions, the hard gun barrel would hit their backs and legs hard. But they can't shout in pain, otherwise, the gun barrel will hit them continuously.

If it is a newly arrived miner, for fear that he will not be able to endure the hardship and escape, he must also be nailed with a pair of thick shackles, which resonate when walking, causing great pain, but once he enters the mine to work, there is no way to resist! And he can't even think about escaping. Mine police are monitoring him from all directions. If he slips, the bullet has already penetrated his head! It is not until five years later that the shackles are removed. By that time, he has been worn down to obedience, and he has gotten used to the life and will not think about escaping, but when he walks, he always waddles in an eight-character pattern, and the brand of the shackles can never be erased!

The mine is deeply buried underground, and the workers have to crawl into the cave with their backs bent; the inside is so dark and humid, so they light up the magnesium lamp and crawl slowly, and wisps of foul smoke spread out, making the turbid air exceptionally suffocating, making everyone unable to breathe. It is not easy to crawl to the place of work, (this place is a little higher and wider.) People then place the magnesium lamp and use all their strength to swing the pickaxe, knocking down pieces of ore and putting them into burlap bags. When they are full, they carry them on their shoulders and crawl out of the cave step by step. The second batch of people will take over and crawl in. This rotation continues until dusk, and people drag their tired bodies back to eat dinner, rest for a while, and then rush to do night work.

Every day, they only eat a meal of brown rice, some salted radish, green vegetables, and soybeans are the unchanging side dishes. The miners all wear copper plates engraved with numbers, and they call each other by numbers. Their names have been forgotten. Working in the mine, everyone is worried about the danger of blasting and flooding. Once this unfortunate incident occurs, people can only close their eyes and wait for death. There is nothing they can do! But the mine owners seem to have no pity for this. If a large number of people die, there will be another large number of workers rushing to fill the vacancies!

The life of a miner is always dark and painful, and the gloomy mine does not know how many skeletons dreaming of golden dreams are buried, but only the mine owner with a bulging belly is fed!

Imperial Incense Drifting Record 172

— Original by Princess Deling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

Unfortunately, none of us closed our eyes. The expression on her face clearly told us that the emperors of these two generations really could no longer have any real and sincere image of the Empress Dowager because the years were too far apart. She just treated them like gods and Buddhas in temples, casually fabricating some far-fetched myths for them. However, the relics piled up in this hall are really not few: a large part of them are the robes they wore, piled up in several boxes of various colors, like the costume boxes used by opera troupes; there are also many rings inlaid with precious jade or pearls that they wore during their lives, all contained in glass boxes; and there are also many bowls and dishes, which are said to be the utensils of these two deceased emperors. Although these things are all very ordinary, and not very valuable in terms of value, they can indeed have the power to make future generations have some thoughts of seeing things and thinking about people when used as souvenirs.

These four palaces are connected, and as we walked through them all the way, we have probably walked halfway and have reached the place where Emperor Qianlong's relics are stored. We know the most about Emperor Qianlong's life, and compared to all the relics left by the emperors of the past in these four halls, Emperor Qianlong's part is naturally the most glorious. Therefore, we all have a special sense of importance and plan to carefully appreciate the things left by this incomparably wise emperor, which are enough to add a lot of glory to these old palaces.

He has many relics, and the most eye-catching among them is a large oil painting hanging on the central wall, which depicts Emperor Qianlong's portrait. (189)

Economic Supplement

Agricultural Extension Problems 173

— Huang Kutong

The term "agricultural extension," as I recall, has only been commonly used in our country for about ten years. As for its meaning, depending on individual subjectivity, it can be broad or narrow. However, a common understanding is that agricultural extension is a means of improving agriculture, which is a narrow interpretation. If the implementation of agricultural policy is seen as agricultural extension, then it is a broad interpretation. On March 29th of the 22nd year of the Republic of China, the Ministry of Industry, the Ministry of Education, and the Ministry of Interior jointly announced the [Revised Agricultural Extension Regulations] (the original [Agricultural Extension Regulations] were promulgated and implemented in May of the 18th year). Article 1 states: [The National Government, in order to popularize agricultural science knowledge, enhance farmers' skills, improve agricultural production methods, improve rural organization, farmers' lives, and promote farmer cooperation, shall implement agricultural extension in accordance with the provisions of these regulations.] According to this provision, it is self-evident that it belongs to the broad interpretation of agricultural extension. Which of the broad and narrow interpretations is appropriate? There is much to discuss. However, this is not what this article intends to explore, and the focus of the extension problem is not here, so I will leave it aside for now.

Whether agricultural extension is practiced in a broad or narrow sense, in my opinion, the main premises are nothing more than: (1) What is there to extend? (2) In what time and space should extension work be carried out? (3) How can practical results be achieved? I think these are very important issues that should be discussed. In other words, one concerns the material to be extended; the second concerns the environment for extension; and the third concerns the technology of extension. Now, I will briefly state my personal opinions on these three items below.

As far as I know, in agricultural extension, there is often a rush to promote things without asking whether the goods are reliable or whether there is a need for them, which is a dangerous behavior. Why do I say this?

Everyone understands that agriculture in our country must be improved. It is reasonable and appropriate to use extension activities to achieve agricultural improvement. However, if one only pursues the good name of extension and engages in advertising-style exaggeration without first examining one's own goods, that is, without first reviewing whether the things used for extension are genuine and needed in the field of agriculture, then the result will be a great sacrifice. Not only will it fail to achieve the purpose of agricultural improvement, but it will also arouse resentment and rejection from farmers, affecting other extension work and the implementation of all agricultural policies. Therefore, in addition to considering various objective conditions, the things used for extension must first undergo a considerable period of research and experimentation to determine the authenticity of the extension materials before they can be extended and widely adopted, achieving practical results. Therefore, extension and research are closely related, and research should not be based on short-term or localized results to immediately promote widely, which would backfire and obstruct the path of extension. For example, when promoting various improved seeds, one must first ask whether the improved seeds are indeed reliable and have universal suitability. If there is still doubt, they should not be promoted rashly to avoid sacrifice. Speaking of this, we often feel that the current agricultural research institutions and agricultural extension institutions in our country lack the function of connection and a unified consciousness. There is a situation where research is research and extension is extension, which is an event that urgently needs to be improved. In other words, extension institutions should take materials from research institutions and obtain genuine and reliable goods; and research institutions should consult extension institutions to determine the steps of research. Only by advancing together can the effect of improvement be achieved.

Agriculture is subject to the limitations of time and place, that is, its seasonality and locality have a significant effect. It is a simple and obvious principle that agricultural improvement must first examine these two characteristics and find ways to adapt to or overcome them, so I won't say much. However, in fact, there are those who carry out extension work regardless of everything. For example, promoting cotton seeds in non-cotton-producing areas is a futile effort. Moreover, in addition to the natural conditions of time and place that should be investigated, the economic and social conditions have a controlling force on agriculture that cannot be ignored. For example, in the midst of extreme decline in the silk economy, promoting mulberry cultivation is also a futile effort. In short, extension should not be based entirely on subjective views but should take the objective environment of agriculture as a premise, with careful planning and long-term consideration, to avoid sacrifice, which is the right way to do things. Some people who specialize in agricultural natural sciences often deny or do not understand economic and social conditions and seek to promote their research results, which is a scientific game. Chinese agriculture has already become an integral part of world agriculture, and the news of its rise and fall is becoming increasingly complex. It would be extremely ridiculous to implement agricultural extension with eyes closed and doors shut!

The target of agricultural extension is mainly farmers. If farmers deny everything, then it cannot be extended, let alone widely adopted. Therefore, whether farmers can accept extension work is a major issue. Everyone knows that most farmers in our country are ignorant and conservative, selfish and stubborn, and always suspicious of new things and difficult to accept. However, this is not an absolutely unchangeable nature. If extension work can indeed bring benefits to farmers, why wouldn't they be happy to do it? As far as I know, some extension activities do not take into account the interests of farmers themselves, nor do they consider their economic power. They are merely embellished, exaggerated, or even deceptive and oppressive. Then, it is inevitable that farmers will feel resentment and reject them. Therefore, in my opinion, in addition to considering the two issues of the material to be extended and the environment for extension, the technical issues in the implementation of extension are also very important. This is a human issue and absolutely cannot be ignored. Having the things and getting the opportunity, it is also necessary to have good people to promote them, otherwise the goal will not be achieved, and bad results will be obtained. The organization of agricultural extension implementation is ultimately a human issue (of course, the funding issue cannot be ignored). It is best to have graduates from agricultural schools do extension work, but those who have become urbanized are not suitable. Those who only have knowledge from books and lack practical experience are also not suitable. Those who have no sympathy for farmers, despise rural life, and cannot endure hardship are especially unsuitable. In this way, it is not easy to find a group of suitable extension personnel. No matter how complete the upper-level organization of the extension agency is, if there is a lack of good roles in the lower-level work, then the so-called agricultural extension is only in name and inevitably becomes bureaucratic, and farmers are still indifferent to it. As for the training of extension personnel, it is not enough to simply instill knowledge from books or lectures on special topics for three or two months. I think it is best to train them in the rural areas, that is, to select some suitable agricultural school graduates and have experienced and advanced extension personnel lead them to the rural areas, completely living a rural life, doing practical training, and cultivating a group of extension personnel with honest qualities, diligent habits, accurate knowledge, and practical experience, and then let them take on the extension work of a certain village or a certain species. I believe that people trained in this way are much better than students who have just left school, and farmers will inevitably trust them more. However, such personnel must not work in isolation. On the one hand, they should be directed by the extension agency, and on the other hand, they should contact other agencies (such as district and township offices, rural elementary schools, etc.) to seek the welfare of farmers. Since their responsibilities are heavy and their work is tedious, they should be given generous treatment so that they can work hard with peace of mind and stay in their positions for a long time. With suitable people, various extension activities, such as breeding demonstrations, disease prevention, and all other agricultural improvement matters, can be carried out step by step and achieve the expected results.

Above, I have briefly stated the three issues of material, environment, and technology that I consider important in agricultural extension. These three issues are interconnected and can also be viewed separately. Only when the three are connected and suitable can the extension be successful. The reason why agricultural extension in various places cannot achieve good results is, of course, the lack of funding, which is a major reason, but it is also related to the three issues I mentioned above. Even if the funding is sufficient, the regulations are beautifully written, and the organization is well-equipped, if the three issues mentioned above are not fully resolved, agricultural extension will still not work, which is my personal prejudice. As for extension work, it should be carried out systematically and continuously, which goes without saying.

Review of the Japanese Silk Industry (Continued) 174

— Ling Wenqin

The success of the Japanese silk industry, while relying on the precision of trade and the excellence of manufacturing technology, is fundamentally based on sericulture. The extraordinary achievements of sericulture must be attributed to the popularity of education and the efforts of the political world. In recent years, our country has used various methods to persuade farmers to use scientific sericulture, but the results have not been significant, which is also suffering from a lack of education. Although the matter must be successful, it still needs time. Japanese silk factories, with past efforts, have removed almost all difficulties, unlike our country's factories, which are hindered by others everywhere. Since 1931, exporters have no longer been able to nitpick, and middlemen have saved much trouble in negotiations. Japanese silk sales must be inspected by the National Silk Inspection Institute, graded, certified, and delivered at market prices, without any dispute. Although exporters have argued that American customers cannot accept this system, the case has been implemented and there is no reason to change it. Recently, there has been talk of convening a silk grading committee in Tokyo to revise the silk grades. The attendees of this meeting include American users, Japanese exporters, silk manufacturers, and representatives of countries related to world silk.

In Japan, ordinary trade is open. For example, if a certain item is traded for a certain amount today, and who bought it, the newspaper will report it in detail the next day. Therefore, silk brokers (our country's brokers) must bring a detailed list of their goods to the exporters. If they agree to the transaction, they can sign the order and remove the item from the list to show that the transaction has been completed. Therefore, it is easy to see how much business is done in a day.

As for the purchase of raw materials, the cocoon price standard is determined by the government according to the market, and the price rises and falls according to the upper, middle, and lower grades. This is convenient for manufacturers to calculate costs. Japanese silk manufacturers regard the cocoon collection period as the life and death of their business, because all the raw materials they need for the entire period are selected during this short period. At that time, the host must pay attention to the market conditions in Yokohama and New York, and on the other hand, use his sensitive means to call his cocoon collectors and decide which cocoons are most profitable to purchase. The cocoon collectors regard the evaluators as important. Only experienced and deeply knowledgeable people can be competent, because the power of profit and loss is entirely in their hands. The Japanese silk industry attaches more importance to the [Hanging] number (Kaka is the i number) than our country's [Discount] when calculating costs, and it is more accurate. For example, if the standard cocoon price today is 3 yen for a silk content (Momer) of 12 percent, then it is known to be 25 [Hanging] (3 yen multiplied by 100 divided by 12). Then multiply by 16 (Japanese 16 kan equals 1 dan) to know that the raw material cost of each dan of silk is 400 yen. Adding a certain amount of reeling labor, the cost of each dan of silk can be obtained. According to this calculation, it will never change. If there is no hope of rising market conditions in the future, forward contracts can be sold in the exchange for a slight profit, and there is no need to worry about delivery. The method of calculating the cost is as follows:

3. 00×100

11=25 16×25=400

The declining value of silk is affected by the global recession, the decline in American consumption, and the competition of rayon, but the excessive development of Japanese silk, resulting in surplus production, is the root cause. If the silk-producing countries of the world cooperate to limit production in order to make production and consumption appropriate, the selling price may be higher. In the era of industrial and commercial warfare, it is a matter of survival. How can this be done? See the following figures. The difficulties of the Japanese silk industry are ten times greater than ours. In terms of production, 1932 was 40% more than 1923, but the value was 40% lower. The farmers or silk manufacturers bear this loss.

What we are paying attention to in Japanese silk and want to compete with is machine-made silk, that is, Japanese silk exports. Since 1929, the annual output has been more than 620,000 bales, while the United States' annual consumption is less than 600,000 bales. According to this calculation, the output of Japanese machine-made silk is enough to meet the annual needs of the United States, and it can also be transported to Europe for sale. Therefore, the oversupply of silk has already occurred five or six years ago. Unfortunately, at that time, our country's silk factory industry was in the golden age, and no one paid attention to it. In order to facilitate foreign trade, Japan has been devaluing the yen since 1931 and subsidizing exchange losses, so that silk exports can be unimpeded. The sufferer is that Chinese silk has since fallen into decline. I am saddened by the demise of Chinese silk, and I can't help but feel the vicissitudes of life for the Japanese. Looking at its increasing production and decreasing prices, I don't know how to remedy it.

In order to break this depressed silk industry, the Japanese have to find other methods to regulate it. Scholars and silk merchants are panicking all day long, researching and discussing the steps that have been taken: (1) Investigating the needs of various countries for silk goods, silk factories are equipped with silk machines, so the domestic consumption of factory silk has reached about 60,000 bales per year; (2) Reusing cocoons to make silk, dumping them in Southeast Asia, India, and other places; (3) Using cocoons to make artificial wool to reduce the import of Australian wool. According to the current production of spring cocoons, spring silkworms are 7% less than last year, and the new autumn cocoons are estimated to be 28.4% less; it is estimated that the Japanese silk output will be 100,000 bales less. (Note) In Table 3 of the previous review of the Japanese silk industry, under each year, two lines are listed, the numbers on the first line are the number of factories, and the numbers on the second line are the number of machines.

On the Current Relief of Our Country's Match Industry 175

— Si Ren

In China, where light industry is still in its infancy, the match industry can be said to be a very important sector in manufacturing. There are over a hundred match factories nationwide, and hundreds of thousands of people directly and indirectly depend on it for their livelihoods. No matter how society evolves or undergoes changes, matches, since their invention in the 19th century, have maintained their inherent position in all applications. Furthermore, observing from various perspectives, the use of matches will become increasingly common, and social consumption will continue to increase. Although our country's match industry is constantly facing difficulties and cannot be described as deeply rooted, it undeniably has a long history. In the current stage of Chinese industry, everything is showing signs of decline, decay, and bankruptcy. The match industry is, of course, no exception and has helplessly entered its crisis. Internally, there is infighting among competitors; externally, there is the dumping of foreign goods, leading to decline and stagnation, increasingly becoming precarious. If efforts are not made to provide relief and gradually improve the situation, and establish a solid foundation for our country's nascent industry, then the match industry, which has a slight position in impoverished industries, will likely follow agriculture and cotton yarn and be on the verge of bankruptcy!

Upon investigation, our country's initial matches were all imported from foreign countries. During the Tongzhi and Guangxu periods of the Qing Dynasty, the matches used in our country were mostly imported from Europe. It wasn't until the 22nd year of Guangxu that Japanese matches began to be imported. The main export ports of Japan were Osaka and Kobe. The matches produced there were sold in the Northeast, North China, and along the Yangtze River, earning considerable profits for a time. Later, the Japanese, based on the Treaty of Shimonoseki, intensified their efforts and established factories in our country's treaty ports to manufacture. At that time, generally knowledgeable people in our country, considering the outflow of money and loss of rights, and because the scale of the match industry was relatively small and easier to operate, also gathered funds to establish factories. The first was the Juchang Match Company in Chongqing, Sichuan, making that company the pioneer of our country's match industry. Since then, match factories have been established in various provinces across the country, such as the Xiechang Match Company in Hankou, the Hefeng Match Company in Changsha, and the Xiechang Match Company in Shanghai. When the European War broke out and after the May Fourth Movement, the people rose up to resist Japanese goods and, recognizing the urgency of revitalizing industry and recovering rights, the establishment of domestic match factories surged like a spring after rain, seemingly replacing imported goods. That period can be said to be the golden age of the match industry. However, after this period, the situation deteriorated rapidly, becoming irreversible. The match factories with larger capital were still able to maintain some composure, while those with smaller capital were stretched to their limits, revealing their embarrassment. By the 22nd year of the Republic, more than ten small factories had been unable to maintain operations and had closed down.

The gradual decline of our country's match industry began in the 16th year of the Republic, and the situation was extremely precarious in the 17th and 18th years, seeming on the verge of collapse. By the 19th year of the Republic, the Xiechang, Zhonghua, Hongsheng, and Yusheng match factories began to merge, and after the establishment of the Greater China Match Company, market prices gradually rebounded, showing some signs of recovery for a time. By the end of the 20th year, all factories had profits. Therefore, in the 21st year, a considerable number of new match factories were established. According to people in the match industry, in the 21st year of the Republic, 92 domestic match trademarks were added, and 11 match factories were added. New factories were established in all major cities across the country, totaling over a hundred. The distribution is as follows:

Location Number of Factories Location Number of Factories Location Number of Factories Location Number of Factories Hunan One

Shandong Nineteen Guangdong Five Jilin Six Liaoning Five Jiangxi One

Jiangsu Nine Sichuan Nine Hebei Six Henan Four Guangxi One

Zhejiang Four Yunnan Four Shanxi Three Fujian Three Guizhou One

Shaanxi Two Gansu Two Anhui Two Hubei One Heilongjiang One

Among these hundred or so factories, the Greater China Match Company has the strongest capital and the largest scale. The company currently has a capital of two million yuan. Others such as the Jinan Zhenye Company, Qingdao Huabei Company, Macau Riri Company, Beiping Danhua Company, and Hangzhou Guanghua Company all have capital ranging from 200,000 to 1 million yuan. Among them, the output of Greater China is also the largest, producing about 10,000 boxes per month, 50 gross per box, and an annual output of about 6 million gross. Combined, all domestic factories can produce millions of boxes annually. However, according to expert estimates, the annual consumption of matches nationwide is no more than 600,000 to 700,000 boxes. Considering the production situation in the seven provinces of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Shandong, Hunan, Hubei, and Jiangxi, the total match production from July of the 20th year to June of the 21st year was 562,000 boxes. From July of the 21st year to June of the 22nd year, it increased to 700,000 boxes. In one year, the total output of the seven provinces increased by 140,000 boxes, but the consumption of matches in the seven provinces has not increased so rapidly, resulting in an oversupply of matches. We already know that if demand exceeds supply, prices rise; if supply exceeds demand, prices fall. This is an immutable principle of economics. Therefore, the market price of matches has greatly declined. According to investigations, in March of the 21st year of the Republic, top-grade large-box matches were 59 yuan per box, second-grade medium-box matches were 50 yuan per box, and third-grade medium-box matches were 48 yuan per box. By July of the 22nd year, top-grade large-box matches had fallen to 47 yuan per box, second-grade medium-box matches had fallen to 38 yuan per box, and third-grade medium-box matches had fallen to 34 yuan per box, but sales still did not improve. Large factories were barely maintaining, and small factories with simple scales could not sustain operations and declared bankruptcy. Even those that had not declared bankruptcy were in great pain, either being acquired by foreign merchants or preparing to close down. Therefore, the current state of the match industry is extremely precarious, even worse than the precarious situation in the 17th and 18th years!

Upon investigation, the main reason why our country's match industry has been declining and becoming stagnant is that manufacturers have been producing in large quantities without limits, leading to overproduction and low market prices. However, the systematic dumping policies implemented by foreign match merchants, attempting to monopolize the match market and compete fiercely with Chinese match merchants, are also the main reason for the oversupply of Chinese matches. Tracing back to the Tongzhi and Guangxu years, European matches were the first to be imported into our country, followed by Japanese matches. After that, factories were established in China to manufacture. Since then, European matches have gradually decreased. When the European War broke out, the import of European matches into our country almost disappeared. Only after the end of the European War did European goods return to the East, but in small numbers. In the 8th year of the Republic, the import of Swedish matches into our country was only 2,960 taels of silver, but the increase was rapid and astonishing. Swedish matches accounted for the majority. The following lists the quantity and value of foreign match imports in the past ten years:

Year Import Quantity (Unit: Gross) Import Value (Unit: Taels)

Republic 12 2,141,126 93,422

13 2,734,883 1,120,828

14 2,855,296 1,153,131

15 3,703,130 1,455,870

16 6,025,850 2,452,132

17 6,426,966 2,173,743

18 8,412,642 3,316,242

19 8,508,194 3,664,061

20 2,525,125 1,161,374

21 366,588 232,735

22 (October) 61,278

Observing these historical statistics of match imports, since the 12th year of the Republic, the increase has been rapid. In the 16th year of the Republic, it almost doubled compared to the 15th year. The highest was in the 19th year, reaching 3,664,061 taels of Customs silver. However, since the 20th year, match imports have greatly decreased, about one-third of the 19th year. This is because the new tax rate implemented in January of the 20th year, increasing tariffs, imposed a 40% tax rate on foreign matches, leading to a decrease in imports and lower numbers. This phenomenon, on the surface, seems to indicate that foreign goods imports have decreased, and Chinese match merchants have been able to rise. But the reality is not so. Foreign match merchants, seeing that the Chinese government has increased tariffs, and the cost of matches has inevitably risen, and that they would not profit from high selling prices, have improved shipping routes and shifted from importing matches to establishing factories in China to manufacture. This saves transportation costs and import tariffs. As a result, a considerable number of foreign merchants have established match factories in our country. In addition, foreign merchants have strong capital, excellent machinery, fast production, and high-quality products. In the 22nd year, foreign merchants accounted for 18.6% of the match production in Henan and Shandong, and 13.5% in Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui. Their momentum is overwhelming. Furthermore, foreign merchants' match factories in China are subsidized by their governments. Therefore, although their products are excellent and far superior to Chinese matches, their selling prices are lower than Chinese matches. Foreign matches are about 4 or 5 yuan, or even 6 yuan cheaper per box. The average selling price per box is only about 40 yuan, almost a tenth cheaper. It is clear that they intend to monopolize the market and put Chinese match merchants to death. Chinese match merchants are at this critical juncture of survival. If they continue to procrastinate and do not seek relief, foreign match merchants will seize our country's market, and the road to bankruptcy for Chinese match merchants may not be far away.

Speaking of the relief of today's match industry, it is not an easy task. Externally, there are strong enemies; internally, there is infighting among competitors. Therefore, how to defeat this current strong enemy and how to avoid infighting among competitors are the two major issues in rescuing the match industry. If foreign matches can be defeated, domestic matches can rise. If infighting among competitors is avoided, they can work together in harmony to seek development. I believe that the way to relief is that, on the one hand, the government should strongly protect the industry; on the other hand, manufacturers must sincerely unite to stem the tide before it arrives. The methods of relief can be roughly divided into the following points:

(1) Implement Anti-Dumping Taxes. For the sake of protecting industries, the state should levy severe tax rates on foreign matches. For those foreign merchants who establish factories in China to manufacture, all types of matches they produce must be registered, and the trademarks, quality, selling prices, etc., should be clearly stated. Any foreign matches that are sold cheaply below their cost should be subject to special anti-dumping taxes to protect domestic matches. Those who do not register and sell without authorization should be prohibited from selling nationwide.

(2) Restrict Foreign Merchants from Establishing Factories. Foreign merchants establishing factories in China to manufacture matches generally have three benefits: (A) They can hire cheap Chinese labor; (B) They can use cheap Chinese raw materials; (C) Once manufactured, they can sell locally, avoiding high tariffs, transportation costs, etc. Therefore, their products are cheap and of good quality, making it impossible for our country's match factories to compete. Therefore, strict restrictions should be imposed. However, the establishment of foreign match factories is based on the commercial treaties signed in the past, and the locations of the factories are mostly in concessions where our country's laws do not apply. Therefore, the implementation of this point is very difficult. However, it is necessary to promulgate and implement measures such as requiring match factories to register with our government. If, after strict review, it is found that there are various issues, our government should not approve it and prohibit its establishment.

(3) Reduce Import Taxes on Raw Materials. Although our country's match industry is constantly facing difficulties, it has made significant progress in recent years, such as the establishment of domestic Huachang match splint factories in Pudong, Shanghai. Therefore, most match raw materials can already be self-sufficient and do not need to rely on foreign countries. There are several types of match raw materials, such as red phosphorus, potassium chlorate, sulfur, and paraffin oil, which are not yet manufactured domestically. Therefore, the government should review the situation and reduce tax rates on the import of these necessary raw materials, and eliminate various handling fees to reduce costs, promote sales, and compete with foreign matches.

(4) Expand Markets. According to experts, our country can currently produce one million boxes of matches annually, but domestic consumption is only over 600,000 boxes, less than 700,000 boxes, resulting in an oversupply situation, as mentioned earlier. Therefore, to achieve a balance between production and sales, and match supply and demand, it is necessary to expand sales and develop overseas markets. The nearest place would be the Nanyang Islands. The Nanyang Islands are actually the destination for Swedish matches. The foreign matches that are popular in our country are also mostly Swedish matches. Therefore, Swedish matches have a hidden dominant position in the match industry. To compete with this powerful hegemon, it is necessary to improve quality and lower prices; otherwise, it may be ineffective.

(5) Improve Quality. Improving the quality of matches is the most important task for the match industry today. In the past, our country's matches were once sold in Manila, Philippines, but were not welcomed by the local people because (A) it was easy for the entire box of matches to ignite when striking one; (B) it was difficult to light; (C) the manufacture of matches was not good, the match sticks were easily broken, and the chemicals on the matches were not uniform, among other reasons. Recently, it has been heard that the products of the Greater China Match Company are being sold in the Nanyang area, and the future is promising, because the products of that factory have white match sticks, are neatly arranged, and are easy to light. It is hoped that other match factories in our country will also make great improvements to promote sales.

(6) Merge Small Factories. Although there are currently over a hundred match factories in our country, very few have capital of over 500,000 yuan, and even fewer have over 1 million yuan. Small factories lack thorough management, and costs are very high. Therefore, to achieve large-scale production, there must be large-scale match factories with strong capital and excellent products. Management will be less troublesome, and costs will be lower than if small factories operate independently. Therefore, domestic match factories with weak capital should be merged.

In summary, the above points can be obtained. Other measures, such as greatly promoting and encouraging the public to use domestic goods, can also be a method of relief. In short, at this time, time is pressing. If relief is not provided, our country's match industry will be on its last legs and completely ruined. Whether the relief can be effective depends entirely on whether the government can open a way out for domestic industries, and whether match merchants can unite in spirit and work together in harmony!

Commercial News

Overnight Call Loan Rate Suddenly Drops by 1.5% 177

The financial market situation, since entering this month, due to the end of the general closing period, coupled with the forced temporary abandonment of export cash due to the general trend, the market situation has tended to ease. Yesterday was also Sunday, causing the overnight call loan rate to suddenly drop by 1.5%, changing to 0.2%. Last Week's Government Bonds on the Securities Exchange Rose and Fell with the Overnight Rate 179

The Market Was Closed on Wednesday Due to Settlement

January Futures Debuted on Thursday

The Market Prices of Near-Term and Far-Term Contracts Were Similar

The Transaction Volume Reached 10,000,000 Yuan

Last week, from November 26th to December 1st, the Huashang Securities Exchange's November futures trading was suspended. The January futures trading began on the 29th. During the week, fluctuations were mostly affected by the high and low overnight rates. The environment was more stable than before. For example, the great success of suppressing bandits, the gradual consolidation of the situation in North China, and the exchange of envoys between the Central Government and the Southwest, making it not difficult to realize the grand reunion. The previous decline in the government bond market was entirely due to the tightness of credit. The outflow of cash is not just beginning now. The previous deposits in foreign banks were an intangible outflow, while the current shipments to foreign countries are a tangible outflow. As inflows are far exceeded by the large outflows, the outflow of cash is difficult to stop. However, the amount of cash being sent to the interior by the military recently to meet commercial needs is also very large. The Shanghai cash reserves are scarce, which is an undeniable fact. The decrease in cash increases the overnight rate, and too high an overnight rate obstructs the circulation of government bonds. Although this is the case, it is not serious and can be considered a temporary phenomenon. The future of the overnight rate is expected to ease, but it is difficult to recover, so market prices are not affected by this shock, and the prices fluctuate within a constrained range. During the week, the government bond market experienced large fluctuations. Initially, the price fell due to the gradual rise in the overnight rate and the increasing tightness of credit. Then, the price rose due to the slight easing of the overnight rate, the good environment, and the return of cash. The rapid changes were exhausting for both long and short positions. On Monday, the November contract had already been suspended, and there was no need to cover short positions urgently. The overnight rate was high again, and the bulls exited, causing the price to fall throughout the day, from a small amount of jiao to 1.2 yuan. On Tuesday, the overnight rate was high again, and number 11 was frantically expensive, while number 4 slightly covered short positions. The market price was slightly chaotic, with high and low prices intermingling, ranging from 2 to 3 jiao. On Wednesday, the overnight rate was the highest at 0.4%, but trading was suspended for the settlement of October futures. On Thursday, the overnight rate did not move, and January futures trading began. Many far-term contracts were bought, and there was a rumor that HSBC was returning cash, boosting confidence. This was also a reaction to the recent weakening market. After an initial fall, the market price rebounded sharply, rising sharply from several jiao to 1.5 yuan. Numbers 50 and 53 were very aggressive in buying. On Friday, the overnight rate stabilized and gradually eased, and the price rose again by 1 to 2 jiao to 0.7 jiao. On Saturday, the market stabilized, and although the overnight rate slightly eased, most of the buying orders were satisfied, and the market transactions decreased, with prices slightly better by 2 to 3 jiao. However, there was a sudden rumor that number 96 would not be paid, which was an unreasonable rumor and not worth laughing at. Therefore, number 96 alone fell by 0.6 jiao. The market situation was such that the far-term prices were almost the same as the near-term prices, which shows that new long positions were increasing in the far-term contracts. With such high interest rates, arbitrage is not possible, which indicates the tightness of credit. The spot market may ease, but the overnight rate may ease or rise. Therefore, the price cannot fall due to the current situation, and the price is constrained by the overnight rate, so it may hover. The number of storage is estimated to be about 6.6 million, mostly held by large short positions. There are many scattered small long positions. The short positions are held by numbers 16, 21, 23, 33, 38, 43, and 78, totaling 3.6 million, and the long positions are held by numbers 3, 9, 14, and 35, totaling 1.6 million, with the rest scattered among various accounts. The week's market price resulted in a slight increase of several jiao, except for number 96, which fell by 7.5 jiao. The total transaction volume was 10,000,005,600 yuan, and 10 shares of stock.
