Suggestions for Medical Case Jury System 183

— Song Guobin

Qin Zhen, Vice President of the Judicial Yuan, went to Europe to investigate the judicial systems of various countries. Upon returning to China the other day, he submitted a written opinion to the government on improving China's judicial system. His suggestions, totaling nine items, all hit the nail on the head, and the pilot implementation of a jury system is one of them.

Qin stated: [The jury system originated in England and has been promoted in European and American countries. Its function is, on the one hand, to assist the court in investigating matters, reducing the labor of judges, and on the other hand, to prevent judges from overstepping their authority and indiscriminately detaining the innocent, thereby protecting the freedom of the people...]

After carefully reading the above text, the importance of the jury system is self-evident. The responsibilities of jurors can be summarized into two points: (1) to assist the court in investigating matters, and (2) to prevent judges from overstepping their authority. Excellent words! Every word hits the mark. Speaking as a medical professional, I would like to discuss the reasons why a jury system must be implemented in medical cases.

Recently, medical disputes have been increasing day by day, with a momentum that is surging and unstoppable. The courts handling these cases and the accused doctors recognize that medicine is a highly specialized field that cannot be fully judged by ordinary legal provisions. Therefore, they often request formal medical institutions in the country to provide academic assessments of the case's circumstances. This type of assessment work is in line with Qin's statement of "assisting the court's investigation and reducing the labor of judges," which is the initial step towards a jury system. However, these written assessments are merely documentary evidence. It is uncertain whether judges will base their judgments solely on these documents. If the judge still adopts an arbitrary attitude, wouldn't this assessment work be in vain, and wouldn't the grievances of the medical community be difficult to eliminate? It must be understood that judges base 30-40% of their judgment on the reasons stated in the complaint, and 60-70% on the arguments presented in court. If the reasons in the complaint are sufficient, but the arguments in court are limited by eloquence, or the judge's questions fail to grasp the key points, then a loss is still unavoidable. Therefore, the jury of experts is of utmost importance. For the sake of upholding justice and redressing grievances, in addition to the written assessment from formal medical institutions, we should further demand a jury. The qualifications of jurors should be scholars who are well-versed in medicine and also knowledgeable in law, so that they can assist the judge in areas where the judge's inquiry is insufficient and correct the judge's tendency to sympathize with either party. Only in this way can we achieve Qin's goal of "preventing judges from overstepping their authority and protecting the freedom of the people." I dare to briefly write down my views for the judicial and administrative authorities to consider!

A Discussion on the Health and Medical Situation in Huaiyin (Part 2) 184

— Xu Fangyou

(5) Old Medical Profession: Traditional Chinese medicine still holds a dominant position in today's society. In Huaiyin, excluding the rural areas, there are about 60 to 70 traditional Chinese medicine practitioners inside and outside the city. In the early years of the Republic of China, there was an organization called the Huaiyin Medical Research Association, with about 30 members. In 1924, it was reorganized into the Huaiyin Medical and Pharmaceutical Research Association, with the same number of members. Recently, stimulated by the regulations on the management of traditional Chinese medicine issued by the provincial government, they submitted a request to the Party headquarters to organize the Huaiyin National Medicine Association and are actively proceeding with it. It was officially established on the 23rd of this month, with about 60 members.

Since the Republic of China, there has been no official medical bureau for traditional Chinese medicine. In the early years of the Republic of China, local people raised funds to provide medical care and medicine at the Ci Yun Temple outside the city during the summer. Later, it was suspended due to lack of funds. In recent years, the Qingjiang Jisheng Branch has been extending medical treatment and medicine for three months every summer.

(6) Old Pharmaceutical Industry: Traditional Chinese medicine shops today will inevitably be eliminated on the one hand, but on the other hand, there are also aspects worth improving. There are about 20 traditional Chinese medicine shops inside and outside Huaiyin City. They are all stuck in their old ways, and even the process of preparing prescriptions according to the formulas may not be followed by everyone. If this continues, regression is a concern. It depends on the self-awareness of those in this industry.

The traditional Chinese medicine industry has the Huaiyin Pharmaceutical Industry Association, which is merged with the new pharmaceutical industry as a member of the Chamber of Commerce. However, it is recently rumored that it will merge with the newly established National Medicine Association. It is unknown whether this will be realized.

(7) Emerging Medical Institutions: 1. Kala-Azar Research Team. Kala-azar, commonly known as "痞塊病," has been spreading widely in northern Jiangsu in recent years. It is rampant in counties such as Huaiyin, Lianshui, Siyang, Guanyun, Donghai, Suqian, and Tongshan. Since the beginning of this spring, the Ministry of Health has specially sent Section Chief Yao Yongzheng, technician Huang Kegang from the Health Experiment Office, and specialist Dr. Vogel, a German professor from the University of Hamburg, Germany, to conduct on-site investigations in various counties in northern Jiangsu. They arrived in Huaiyin on January 13th and then went to various counties under Huai, Hai, and Xu, as well as Huaiyuan and Fengyang counties in Anhui Province, for a week of investigation. They returned to Beijing to report. After deliberation between the Ministry of Health and the Health Experiment Office, it was decided to establish an institution for the prevention and treatment of Kala-azar in Huaiyin. On the one hand, it will treat existing patients, and on the other hand, it will engage in academic research. Once the transmission route is determined, the area for promoting prevention and treatment work will be planned. The intention is very good. Therefore, in May, the Ministry of Health sent Section Chief Yao Yongzheng and Dr. Pu Nan'gu to Huaiyin to survey the site and prepare everything. It was officially announced on June 20th. The team is located at the former site of the People's Hospital, with the main entrance opening into the Provincial People's Education Center, occupying more than 20 rooms. Currently, Dr. Pu Nan'gu and Dr. Sun Zhirong serve as the director and deputy director, respectively, in charge of medical affairs. There are also assistants, nurses, staff, and servants, totaling about a dozen people. It is equipped with consultation, surgery, medication preparation, testing, animal, and refrigeration rooms. Because the team focuses on research and provides treatment as an adjunct, there are only six hospital beds available. Everything is free of charge. Outpatient service is held every other day, limited to six numbers each time, with a maximum of ten numbers, also completely free of charge. It is said that in the four months since its establishment, it has treated about 500 people. It is hoped that the team will continue to work hard in the future, expand its scope, and identify the transmission route of Kala-azar as soon as possible, so that prevention can be carried out skillfully. At the same time, we ask all parties to assist with funding and establish more free treatment institutions in the epidemic area of northern Jiangsu. The merit would be immense.

2. County-run Drug Addiction Treatment Center: The center began preparations at the beginning of this month. Xu Xianqing was appointed as the director by the Provincial Anti-Smoking Association. The center is located in the Qingjiangpu Branch of the Chinese Red Cross Society. It is divided into consultation, medication preparation, convalescence, and testing rooms. Everything is still being arranged.

(8) Conclusion: The above is the recent health and medical situation in Huaiyin. There is no progress to speak of. Fortunately, the current governor of Jiangsu Province values health matters quite highly. It is hoped that in the near future, there will be a comprehensive plan for health administration and medical undertakings in various places to promote them. The people of Huaiyin can also enjoy the benefits of the government's promotion of public health. I can't help but look forward to it.

A Medical Perspective on [A Married Man Committing Adultery] 185

— Chen Baoqin

The preference for sons over daughters has been a long-standing practice in China for thousands of years, and it is also a common phenomenon in autocratic countries. Because power is held in the hands of one person, all regulations are naturally aimed at satisfying personal desires, treating women as toys or commodities, and depriving them of their rights almost entirely. The law even stipulates special punishments for women, pushing this to the extreme. Fortunately, since the establishment of the Republic, under the guidance of Sun Yat-sen, women have begun to see a glimmer of hope for restoring freedom. The principle of equality between men and women is enshrined in his will. Just as the revolution is about to be completed today, and men and women jointly bear the responsibility of the country in terms of rights and obligations, it is unexpected that this revision of legislation has produced something unexpected.

Since the Legislative Yuan amended the draft Criminal Law, passing Article 221, Paragraph 2 "[Sexual intercourse with a woman under the age of fourteen shall be considered rape]" and Article 239 "[A married woman who commits adultery shall be sentenced to imprisonment for up to one year; the adulterer shall be subject to the same punishment]," how delighted and jubilant will those who specialize in playing with women be, shouting "Long live the legislators! Long live male rights!" They may think that they can indulge from now on, in brothels, doing whatever they want. If their wives advise them a little, they can raise their voices and say, "This is a right specially granted by national law. How can you interfere?"

On the surface, victory indeed belongs to men, but in reality, it is leading men down the path of all evils. It is tantamount to national legislation encouraging people to throw themselves into the net of the law and harm themselves.

People know that opium is enough to ruin the country and exterminate the race, and violators are all legal criminals. Therefore, the number of prisoners in prison today who violate opium laws is the largest. The legislators did not remove the law because there were many offenders. Why is it said that punishing [married men] will inevitably lead to many violators? In order to avoid the problem of prisons being overcrowded, they stop eating because they are choked, and fundamentally cancel the law. Is this acceptable? Today's prisons are almost entirely occupied by opium offenders; later arrivals will have no room to insert their feet, so the opium ban can also be abolished.

Lowering the age of rape for women is indeed a violation of women. The standard for female maturity is the onset of menstruation. China's land is vast, and due to climatic conditions, very few women under the age of fourteen have their period. How can a few represent the majority? Women who encounter this misfortune account for a very small percentage, while men who contract venereal diseases due to adultery are numerous. Their impact on personal health and the soundness of the nation is extremely great and significant.

I am a doctor, so I know more details. I have clearly indicated that I am a female doctor, and I have not written a venereal disease specialty, but according to the statistics of my clinical consultations, patients with venereal diseases among male and female patients account for more than 60% of the total number. In Chinese customs, it is natural for women to consult female doctors for diseases, but it is surprising for men with venereal diseases to seek treatment from me in the eyes of those without medical knowledge. Then those male doctors who specialize in venereal diseases must have crowded waiting rooms. Moreover, the disease statistics of the Nanjing Municipal Health Office also show that venereal diseases have the highest rate. It can be seen from this that the spread of venereal diseases is so wide that it can be said to have penetrated the people. How it is contracted, there is no need to elaborate. This is due to the lack of moral cultivation of individuals and the lack of interference from national law.

Observing each patient who comes, with a worried face, staggering gait, ashamed and remorseful, and timid speech, the hidden pain and unavailing repentance in their hearts can be imagined. Looking at the affected area, there is pus flowing from the urethra like a small channel, the foreskin is swollen and ulcerated, and urination is like stinging and burning, with fresh blood flowing down. Or frequent urination, dozens of times a day, involuntarily flowing out. Or blocked and impassable, the bladder is swollen, and it is difficult to drip down. Or the testicles are swollen and painful. Afterwards, they are often unable to bear children. Some even have swollen knees and cannot walk. All of this is the general outline of "gonorrhea." As for "syphilis," in the initial stage, sores or ulcers appear in the genital area. In the second stage, rashes appear all over the body, with headaches, bone pain, increased body temperature, and loss of appetite. In the third stage, it penetrates into the bone marrow or pierces the top of the head and nasal bones, expanding and ulcerating, with a foul odor, commonly known as "opening the skylight." Or it invades the spinal cord, and the legs and feet cannot move, becoming paralyzed. Or it enters the internal organs and becomes a tumor. Or it corrodes the blood vessel wall, forming an aneurysm, which ruptures suddenly, causing death in an instant; some even need to have their limbs sawn off. Or the blood vessels harden, easily leading to stroke. Or the heart valves corrode, becoming incomplete closure. Many internal and surgical diseases are caused by syphilis, which is beyond what ordinary people can imagine. In addition, there is "soft chancre," in addition to small ulcers in the genital area, there is also swelling of the inguinal lymph nodes, called buboes. At this time, the body feels cold and hot, with severe pain, making walking difficult, and its maturity and ulceration cannot be cured in a day or two. The symptoms, course, and complications of the above diseases are described in detail in special books. Today, I will only

Page 18

speak of the general outline, so that the general public can know a little and be alert, because patients often cry bitterly and weep to the heavens and call out to their parents when they are in great pain after getting sick, but it is too late! Can the law protect them at this time? Can germs know that they are male and not attack them?

Even more unfortunately, it is transmitted to his wife, so his wife suffers this pain innocently. It also affects the offspring. After a woman contracts "gonorrhea," in addition to the urethra, the vagina is an important colony. At this time, if she gives birth to children, their eyes can be infected with gonococcus when passing through the birth canal, resulting in blindness. Ascending from the vagina to the uterus causes gonorrhea cervicitis, the pain of which need not be mentioned. After becoming chronic inflammation, although she can conceive, she is more likely to miscarry in the second or third month. Ascending further to become gonorrhea salpingitis is the main cause of only having two children or infertility after miscarriage. Infants born to syphilis patients often die young, or the fetus dies in the womb after seven or eight months of pregnancy.

The aforementioned all have a great relationship with the health of the race and the survival of the nation. Therefore, those who have a spouse and commit adultery are even more harmful. It is not only personal harm to the body and mind, waste of money, loss of reputation, impact on career, destruction of family happiness, and being spurned by society.

In addition, there are those who are often encountered in daily clinical consultations, that is, patients who ask doctors to perform induced abortions for them. This is naturally rejected by formal doctors, while general quacks and ignorant midwives are only interested in profit and use unscientific methods, and the deaths of women as a result are also reported in the newspapers every day. Other tragedies caused by adultery are too numerous to mention.

Today, some male legislators believe that only punishing women is to protect male rights and benefit men. They do not know that they are setting a trap to trap them and to trap the entire Chinese nation. If the law stipulates that those who have a spouse and commit adultery shall be sentenced to imprisonment, then the general male, even if not out of fear of crime, will avoid it in order to avoid being dragged into court by his wife, and thus be restrained. As a result, the spread of venereal diseases will be greatly reduced invisibly, and the soundness of the race can be expected. How can some legislators have no medical knowledge and lack social vision to this extent?

Common Sense Q&A about Diseases 186

— Cheng Hanzhang

(46) Nervous Indigestion and Gastric Neurosis

(Q) What is called nervous indigestion?

(A) It is a digestive disorder that occurs due to the influence of the nervous system, while the digestive organs themselves do not have any lesions.

(Q) What is this disease called in Western languages?

(A) In English, it is Nervous Dyspepsia, and in Latin, it is Dyspepsia Nervosa.

(Q) How does this disease occur?

(A) It usually occurs in hysteria, neurasthenia, genital diseases, anemia, malaria, etc. In addition, the abuse of tobacco and alcohol, and mental excitement (such as terror, anger, surprise, joy, and sorrow) can all be the causes of the disease. (Q) What are the symptoms of nervous indigestion?

(A) The symptoms of this disease are very complex and not fixed. It often changes within a short period of time. Usually, there is discomfort in the stomach, fullness, pressure, a feeling of tension, and belching. Sometimes there is loss of appetite, nausea, vomiting, etc.

(Q) Are these many symptoms related to food?

(A) It has nothing to do with the nature or amount of food.

(Q) Are there any other obstacles?

(A) There are also mood swings, headaches, dizziness, insomnia, fatigue, and palpitations.

(Q) Is the acidity in the stomach reduced?

(A) Not necessarily, sometimes it is reduced, and sometimes it is very high.

(Q) What is the treatment for nervous indigestion?

(A) First, it is necessary to treat the cause, avoid mental stimuli, and limit alcohol and smoking. Second, conduct nerve strengthening methods, such as hydrotherapy, massage, and electrical therapy. For medications, you can use stomachic, tonic, and sedative drugs.

(Q) What is called gastric neurosis?

(A) This is a general term for functional disorders of the stomach. There are distinctions between sensory gastric neurosis, motor gastric neurosis, and secretory gastric neurosis.

(Q) What is the Western name for gastric neurosis?

(A) In English, it is Gastroneurosis, and in German, it is Magenneurase.

(Q) What are the symptoms of sensory gastric neurosis?

(A) There are symptoms such as stomach pain, hunger, gluttony, abnormally increased appetite, fullness, nervous anorexia, and taste errors.

(Q) What are the symptoms of motor gastric neurosis?

(A) There are symptoms such as nervous vomiting, nervous belching, gastric peristalsis anxiety, gastric motility hyperactivity, pyloric spasm, cardia spasm, rumination, regurgitation, and gastric relaxation.

(Q) What are the symptoms of secretory gastric neurosis?

(A) There are symptoms such as hyperacidity, excessive gastric juice secretion, hypoacidity, lack of gastric juice secretion, and gastric juice leakage.

(Q) How should the treatment of this gastric neurosis be?

(A) It is advisable to first treat the disorders of the nervous system, taking sedatives such as bromide preparations and valerian preparations. For the symptoms that occur, apply symptomatic treatment separately. (End)

Common Sense of Ear, Nose, Throat, and Eye Hygiene 187

— Tang Renjin

(26) Diphtheria (Continued)

Speaking of the complications of throat diphtheria, they can be distinguished into two types: communicable and metastatic inflammation. Now I will talk about them roughly, as follows.

(A) Communicable inflammation: The main inflammations are three, as follows.

(1) Nasal Diphtheria: It usually starts with nasal congestion and vigorous secretions, initially serous, then bloody purulent (the most important point in diagnosing nasal diphtheria). The skin of the upper lip is red and swollen due to the irritation of the secretions flowing out of the nasal cavity. There is often a necrotic fragment that detaches from the inflamed nasal mucosa and is discharged outward. If a nasal speculum is used to examine the nasal cavity, a grayish-white linear necrotic tissue can be seen. Nasal diphtheria should never be taken lightly, because many children often die from systemic sepsis or prostration.

(2) Laryngeal Diphtheria: It is a serious complication caused by the spread of pharyngeal diphtheria to the larynx. It is most common in children. Its danger lies in the occurrence of acute laryngeal stenosis symptoms. If the treatment is improper or too late, most patients die from suffocation.

(3) Otitis Media: When the inflammation involves the middle ear, the patient feels severe pain in the ear, eventually suppurating, turning into a perforation of the eardrum, and even causing various symptoms or dangers.

(B) Metastatic Inflammation: Inflammation belonging to this category is all due to the action of diphtheria toxin. Its main inflammations are five, as follows.

1. Acute nephritis 丨 Most common.

2. The heart is also prone to disorders, and sometimes there is sudden cardiac death.

3. Lungs 丨 Pneumonia symptoms often occur.

4. Polyarthritis 丨 Induces painful swelling in the joints.

5. Skin changes 丨 Such as roseola-like or erythema-like rash, or skin bleeding. (To be continued)

Common Treatment for Fever (10) 188

— Li Xing

Helping Internal Excretion

I have already discussed the importance of helping the skin excrete during a fever. Besides helping the skin, assisting the kidneys in excretion is crucial. Many medications are unnecessary during a fever, except for diuretics. While increased urination cannot entirely eliminate the toxins produced by bacteria, it can help excrete a portion. We know that the urine of febrile patients is often concentrated and has a high specific gravity when the urine volume is low. Thick urine is harmful to the kidneys. Therefore, helping the kidneys excrete more, resulting in dilute urine with a lower specific gravity, protects the kidneys and prevents future nephritis. While there are many medications to help the kidneys excrete, sodium citrate is the most suitable for febrile patients. This medicine aids kidney excretion, thins phlegm, facilitates bowel movements, and increases the body's alkali reserve. We know that the body often has excessive acid during a fever. Increasing the alkali reserve neutralizes the acid, preventing it from causing harm. Maintaining a neutral blood pH is greatly beneficial to the body. This medicine does not impede digestion. However, it can sometimes cause nausea, so it is best taken by mixing one spoonful of the medicine with a glass of water or fruit juice. Lemon juice, orange juice, and grape juice are preferred.

Medication and Treatment of Fever

Reducing Pain: Common antipyretics are essentially anesthetics for fever. Water therapy for fever reduction is fundamentally different from medication. Water therapy reduces fever without diminishing the body's vitality and resistance. However, antipyretic medications reduce both fever and vitality, thus lowering resistance. Therefore, when the fever is exceptionally high, one should not rely solely on antipyretic drugs. These drugs are most useful for relieving headaches, body aches, calming nerves, and promoting sleep. Be careful not to take too much of these medicines. Too much can decrease resistance, cause excessive sweating, or lead to physical exhaustion. The primary goal of using these drugs is to reduce the patient's pain. It is also important to note that pain often occurs at the onset of the illness. Once the pain subsides, antipyretic medications should no longer be taken.

The names of such drugs are countless, with hundreds or thousands available on the market. Advertisements are everywhere. Many are foreign imports, and even more are manufactured domestically. Patients rarely inquire about the ingredients or efficacy of these medicines. I will briefly describe several commonly used antipyretic drugs for readers to study.

(1) Quinine-based Drugs: Most people now know that quinine can reduce fever. It does so by reducing the body's vitality, which in turn lowers the temperature. This drug can also reduce pain and calm nerves, so a small dose can sometimes help febrile patients sleep. It is clear that if a febrile patient does not have significant pain and their nerves are stable, this drug is unnecessary. Furthermore, because this drug reduces the body's ability to resist bacteria, it should not be taken in excess.

(2) Sodium Salicylate, Aspirin, etc.: These drugs are quite effective in reducing muscle and bone pain, joint pain, and headaches, but they should not be taken for extended periods or in excessive doses.

(3) Antipyrine-based Drugs: These drugs are derived from coal tar through analysis or synthesis. The most important ones include menthol, phenacetin, amidopyrine, and pyrimidone. There are many variations of these drugs on the market. While a small dose may be slightly beneficial for pain relief, it is crucial not to take too much. It has been proven that excessive use of these drugs is harmful. When sick with a fever and headache, it is essential to reduce the fever and relieve the headache, but do not forget that the ultimate goal is to restore the body to health quickly. It is unacceptable to reduce a small amount of pain at the expense of reducing the body's resistance, thereby increasing the severity of the illness. Painkillers primarily numb the nerves. The pain is still present, but the patient is unaware of it. It is better to endure some minor pain to allow the illness to resolve safely and quickly.

Emergency Treatment for Fainting

Every patient with a high fever has a chance of fainting. Those caring for them should not simply shed tears when they see the severity of the illness, but should think of ways to help them through the danger. To help them, one must understand their condition and needs. The primary crisis for a patient is circulatory arrest. Blood transports nutrients to all parts and cells of the body while also carrying waste products from these parts to the excretory organs. Just as the paralysis of all transportation in Shanghai would be disastrous, the arrest of circulation is a step toward death for a patient. Circulatory arrest is caused by toxins produced by bacteria that impair the function of the body's cells. Caregivers must know how to recognize the crisis, understand its symptoms, and then think of ways to prevent it and provide emergency treatment.

A lower degree of circulatory arrest causes fainting. A higher degree causes death. Circulatory arrest is primarily caused by the loss of vascular function and secondarily by heart failure. Some diseases, such as diphtheria, are particularly prone to causing heart failure, leading to fainting. In the case of fainting due to vascular dysfunction, the abdominal blood vessels first lose their contractility, causing blood to pool in the internal organs. The skin becomes pale and cold due to lack of blood, and the heart rate increases. As circulatory arrest worsens, the lips and fingertips turn purple, and the pulse becomes irregular, reaching a critical point.

Appropriate treatment includes: (1) Oral or injected cardiotonics, depending on the severity of the condition. (2) If the blood vessels have lost contractility, elevate or lower the foot of the bed to direct blood flow to the lower limbs or back to the upper body. Rub the lower limbs externally, moving the blood toward the feet. Bind the abdomen tightly with a cloth to reduce blood pooling in the abdominal organs. If the heart is failing, in addition to administering cardiotonics, help the patient sit up. If these methods are properly implemented, they can be very effective in bringing the patient back to life.

Recovery Period Care

The end of the fever does not mean the end of treatment. Another part of the treatment is also important. This part of the treatment is to quickly restore the patient to health and their original work. Proper treatment during this process leads to a faster recovery, while improper treatment can not only slow down recovery but also allow other diseases to take advantage. A weakened body is more vulnerable to severe illnesses, which often lead to unfavorable outcomes. Therefore, during the gradual recovery, appropriate treatment methods must be used. The first thing to note is that as the patient gradually recovers, they often feel stronger than they actually are, i.e., "the spirit is willing, but the flesh is weak." They may feel strong, but they are not yet that strong. Therefore, one should not allow the patient to get up too quickly based on their feelings. A common rule to follow is that the number of days of bed rest (or recuperation) after a fever should equal the number of days of fever. For example, if the fever lasted for three days, bed rest should continue for three days after the fever subsides. For fevers that easily become chronic or lead to other illnesses, the recuperation period should be extended. For example, acute rheumatic fever or acute nephritis requires several weeks of bed rest after the fever subsides. Acute myocarditis or tuberculosis requires several months of bed rest after the fever stops. Diseases that can easily lead to other dangerous conditions during recovery, such as diphtheria and nephritis caused by scarlet fever, require several weeks of bed rest even after the patient appears to be no different from a healthy person. Why? Because the toxins from diphtheria can damage the heart, and getting up and moving too quickly after recovery can easily lead to heart failure, resulting in sudden death. Nephritis caused by scarlet fever can be difficult to treat if not handled carefully.

If daily temperature measurements still show a slight fever, special attention should be paid, and it should not be assumed that the patient is completely recovered. A slight fever indicates that there is still inflammation in the body or that another problem has arisen. In such cases, a doctor should be consulted for a thorough examination. Sometimes constipation after illness can also cause a slight fever, which will subside after a bowel movement. Sometimes the slight fever is due to stopping bed rest too early. Extending the bed rest can help the body recover quickly and completely.

A Brief Discussion on Pulmonary Tuberculosis (31) 189

— Hu Jiayan

Chapter 8: Clinical Examination Methods

What does sputum examination involve? According to diagnostics, it includes macroscopic examination, microscopic examination, bacteriological examination, and chemical examination. Among these, chemical examination has a relatively small role in clinical practice. For example, the demonstration of proteins, which was once considered important, is no longer of great value. In pulmonary tuberculosis, except for the fibrotic type, where variations sometimes occur, sputum from the other types contains proteins. Therefore, it is not very helpful in diagnosing the disease. Our classification here includes: A. Macroscopic examination, B. Microscopic examination, and C. Examination for tubercle bacilli. We will now discuss these aspects in detail below.

A. Macroscopic Examination: It is important to understand that the sputum of patients with pulmonary tuberculosis does not have any special macroscopic features that allow for a definitive diagnosis at first glance. It can only provide clues for further investigation. The types of sputum that should be distinguished include mucoid, mucoserous, mucopurulent, purely purulent, and nummular. Mucoid sputum usually disperses at the bottom of the container. The sputum of pulmonary tuberculosis patients is mostly mucoid or mucoserous and not very abundant. If cavities have formed, the sputum is usually mucopurulent. The mucus and pus are not very well mixed, unlike the sputum of patients with bronchitis or bronchiectasis. The mucus appears transparent, while the pus appears yellow or yellowish-green, making them easy to distinguish macroscopically. Sometimes, the pus appears as small scattered clumps within the mucus, or it may form larger masses, resulting in various forms such as linear, spherical, or coin-shaped. This is the origin of the terms "nummular sputum" and "coin-shaped sputum." Additionally, the presence of blood streaks in the sputum, or the presence of black streaks due to the inhalation of coal dust by city dwellers, which may even cause the entire sputum to turn dark gray, can also be observed with the naked eye. Although these are not specific characteristics of the disease, they are indirectly related to it.

B. Microscopic Examination: In the microscopic examination of this disease, the most important and specialized aspect is the presence or absence of tubercle bacilli. These require a staining procedure to be visible, which will be described in detail in the section below. As for unstained specimens, many findings can also be observed under the microscope. Among these, the most important in relation to this disease is the discovery of "elastic fibers." They may appear as individual fibers or as bundles and networks in the sputum. They may be straight or curved. The branching patterns of the network-like forms are very similar to lung tissue. Their presence is mostly evidence of lung tissue destruction and rarely originates from the bronchial wall. Although their presence in the sputum is not as definitive as the presence of tubercle bacilli in diagnosis, it is still very significant. In suspected cases of pulmonary tuberculosis, sometimes the chest examination does not yield much information. However, if elastic fibers are found in the sputum, the lingering doubts will immediately dissipate. We can at least say that the diagnosis of pulmonary tuberculosis will not be far off.

Besides elastic fibers, other components visible under the microscope include mucus strands and globules, alveolar epithelial cells, red blood cells, white blood cells, and amyloid bodies. All of these have a direct or indirect relationship with pulmonary tuberculosis.

When examining the sputum of people suspected of having pulmonary tuberculosis, one thing must not be forgotten: to check for the presence of lung fluke eggs. This parasitic disease is almost unique to East Asia. After the parasite infests the human lungs, it causes various pathological changes. Its symptoms are very similar to those of pulmonary tuberculosis. In the early stages, the patient has a mild cough and expectorates thick, sticky sputum, which contains bright red spots. This is almost indistinguishable from the blood-streaked sputum of pulmonary tuberculosis patients. As time goes on, the cough worsens, and the patient may even experience significant hemoptysis, as well as anemia and dyspnea. Therefore, an accurate diagnosis requires a complete sputum examination. The accurate identification of these two conditions (pulmonary tuberculosis and lung fluke infection) requires a complete sputum examination. This procedure may seem mundane, but it is crucial because the subsequent treatment strategies are entirely different. I hope that readers and patients will not take it lightly!

Free Talk

Starting from the Contradictions of Superstition Itself 190

— Wu Jian

We have done enough to break superstition.

In the past, we used popular lectures, standing on the position of natural science to break it, but the result was no success.

Even now, there are still many people with good intentions, and they are still doing this. For example, solar eclipse, they have long ago announced this event in the newspaper, saying that on a certain day, a certain hour, or even a certain minute, a solar eclipse will definitely be seen in a certain place; Or use extremely popular text to publish the reason of solar eclipse in the publications, hoping that the public can understand one by one. However, when it comes to the time of solar eclipse, the general public, they still have to knock their gongs, put their firecrackers; They are trying hard to save their precious moonlight.

Using natural science to break superstition is not only failed in these places. The biggest failure is that many of those natural science researchers are also superstitious themselves. For example, how many doctors of the Red Cross today do not believe in religion?

This is because; At first, people's superstition was of course due to the inability to control and understand nature; However, that was when society depended on nature. Later, with the advancement of scientific knowledge, people were able to use natural science and technology to dominate nature; This naturally reduces the superstition of the natural world for the general public who have knowledge. However, something that cannot be understood and cannot be controlled comes again; This thing is the society we live in. Social economic panic, as well as terrible wars and revolutions, have become things that we want to avoid but cannot avoid. Here, the source of modern superstition is hidden again. Even changing a method, breaking superstition from the position of social science, is not something that can be done by a superficial action. For example, in Hunan, we once saw thousands of farmers smash all temples and even schools in one go.

However, now, the newly built temples are more luxurious than before. For example, in Guangxi, when the National Revolutionary Army passed by, under the command of military leaders, all the temples were cleaned up. However, now, next to those broken temples without clay bodhisattvas, those farmers who ask for a good harvest and those patients who ask for medicine are still constantly praying and kneeling there [as if they were on it, as if they were on its left and right].

In modern times, [superstition] has completely become a social problem, not a natural problem. It is a problem that arises from the relationship between people, not a problem that arises from the relationship between people and nature. A few years ago, my grandfather died. I wanted not to do Taoist ritual, not to burn paper houses, not to look at Feng Shui, not to choose a date, but my relatives and even neighbors interfered with me. They said: [If you don't believe it, we want to believe it; Your grandfather's uneasiness after death will also affect our uneasiness. ] In the process of this matter, my superstition about nature has been broken; However, because of social relations, that is, my relationship with relatives and neighbors, I was finally succumbed.

Just persuading people to break superstition, this is already a social task. If people want to be superstitious, let them be superstitious, why do we have to persuade them to break it? The reason is that because we and they live in a society, there is a related reason.

For superstition, the most important thing is to see its material origin. In history, we can see; There is a certain kind of society, and there is a certain kind of superstition or religion corresponding to it. In China, we can also see now; In the countryside, the main hope of the general public is to harvest more grains from the land; Therefore, the most basic and most common god in the countryside is called [land]. In the city, the hope of the general public is to live in peace and work happily. They use the city god (or city pool) built with mud to protect their peace and happiness; Therefore, the most important and most common god in the city is called [City God]. Although the city god built with mud has now been demolished in some places, the general public's hope for a secure life and happy work has not yet been guaranteed; Therefore, the Bodhisattva [City God] can still exist widely. The public's hope for [City God] now is still hoping that he can [protect one side].

In short, superstition, it is also a world view: it has some of the same characteristics as any kind of religion and even any kind of philosophy: That is, an explanation of the world in a certain time and space. However, superstition, it is just the most primitive and most basic explanation of the world.

At present, in China, if we want to shoulder the task of breaking superstition; Or to advance a world view stagnating on superstition to a modern world view, we can only start from the material origins of society.

Every performance of superstition is a performance of contradiction: that is, on the one hand, it expresses belief in the spirit, and on the other hand, it expresses requirements for material things. If we want to break that kind of superstition in spiritual belief, unless we can satisfy their requirements materially. Whoever can satisfy the farmers' requirements for harvest is the one who can eliminate the [harvest] in the farmers' superstition; Whoever can satisfy the security of living and working for the citizens materially is the one who can fundamentally eliminate superstition in the city.

The Ulanhotoke Plain 191

— Shi Dai

Autumn, as soon as it arrives in Ulanhotoke, the weather gets cold. The plain is covered in golden colors, and the withered weeds lie dry and yellow on the ground. The northwest wind howls desperately, without stopping day or night, growing fiercer and fiercer. People and livestock alike, assaulted by the cold wind, tremble in their limbs, their agility and freedom completely stripped away by the storm. Everything is rigid and clumsy, as if the wind is deliberately coming to scour and punish the Ulanhotoke Plain.

People wear fur hats that cover their ears and faces, leaving only their eyes and snotty noses exposed. Although their mouths are hidden in the fur, they pull the hat strings down to their chins when out of the wind, and warm breaths are exhaled from their mouths.

Every morning, the old people kneel straight before the [Living Buddha], praying:

"Living Buddha, protect our livestock and give us warm sunshine!"

The biting cold wind is like a mad beast, howling fiercely across the bare Ulanhotoke Plain. Frozen clouds fly in the sky, and the sun, like a malnourished person, stares listlessly at the plain, the weeds, the livestock, the yurts, and the purple people.

The gurgling sound of the Tashinur River has long disappeared; everyone knows that the sound is hidden beneath a thin layer of ice.

The wind gets stronger every day, and the cold burns across the Ulanhotoke Plain, burning fiercely. It looks like it's about to snow. For the safety of their livestock, the people who graze on the Ulanhotoke Plain are forced to look for places that are "sheltered from the wind and facing the sun." The Ulanhotoke Plain has no mountains in front or ridges behind; the wind from the Gobi Desert sweeps over it without anything to block it. Everyone knows that if they stay here through the winter, the livestock will definitely be blown away by the storm. Maybe the flocks of sheep and even the tents will disappear in the howling wind.

"No matter what, we can't spend the winter in Ulanhotoke."

But:

"Where should we go?"

The traces of experience flash back and forth in everyone's minds, and thought is like a rope tying together all the herders of Ulanhotoke.

Rehashing past experiences, fear immediately ripples around them, making them tremble. That terrible storm, it is the herders' only enemy; it deeply paints the herders' lives with tragic colors, these colors like sharp thorns, stabbing the plain, the livestock, the flocks of sheep, the old and young herders.

The old woman mutters to her son:

"It's going to snow! The wind is getting stronger and stronger. Why are you still dithering here instead of moving? Are you waiting for the wind to blow away my old bones?"

Women mutter to men, old people mutter to young people. To avoid unexpected dangers and disasters, who wouldn't want to leave this Ulanhotoke earlier?

However much they grumble, those who listen just listen. It's no use complaining a hundred times a day. Sometimes, when they get annoyed, they ride out to run a lap, to vent the depression in their hearts.

Not forgetting for a moment that the difficulty in moving lies in not being able to find a good place that is "sheltered from the wind and facing the sun."

Worry hangs on people's faces. No one believes that such a large group of people can't think of a sunny place.

One day, a savior falls to Ulanhotoke, that savior shines a crystal light in people's hearts: that is, old man Hailaklun returns from Kukutai and tells everyone:

"No one lives in Ilieshan over there."

Joy lights up the crowd, and beautiful hope leaps in everyone's hearts.

The wind howls, the sky flies with dust, people, livestock, flocks of sheep, begin to stir on the Ulanhotoke Plain.

Local Customs 192

— Xu Ying

A seagoing mail ship, floating on the sea like a small bird, is about to depart. A warning cry stimulates the eardrums of pedestrians. A thick fog permeates the sky, a vast expanse of white enveloping the sky, the water, and the land. On the pier, a crowd of people of different genders is packed together. The sea breeze hits the face like a sponge soaked in gasoline and covered in coal dust.

John and I are in a sampan, unable to make out each other's features clearly. We are both on guard against pickpockets. Experience tells us to be careful every second in the crowd. Losing belongings is a minor matter; perhaps even one's body might be pushed into the deep sea where the sky and water merge, disappearing like a grain of rice sinking into a pond. We gaze remotely at the floating island-like ship, its brilliant lights piercing through the dense fog.

No one can think of a topic to discuss; everyone's heart is as empty and vague as the thick fog. The emotions created in a flesh-and-blood environment spread like electricity among the parting crowd at this moment. I hear someone nearby kissing passionately, murmuring touching short sentences. I smell the pungent odor of machine oil on someone's clothes. Looking at John, I see him turned away, gazing longingly at the shore.

[Sir, would you like some soil?] I suddenly feel a hand tug at my sleeve. Immediately, I swat his hand away, thinking, how can there still be people dealing in illicit goods in a place like this?

[Sir,] the same voice continues, [This is soil from home, soil from home. In case you get homesick, mix it with water...]

I can't see the person's face clearly, but I see a hand offering a paper packet, a sparkling diamond shining on one of the fingers.

[If you are leaving your motherland, soil from home is even more useful.]

The merchant's tone is quite refined. I was about to reach out when a hand snatched the paper packet. Needless to say, that hand was John's. I am surprised that he is normally such a strong person, yet as he is about to step onto a soil layer of a different geological composition, he can't help but feel attached to his native soil.

[How much?] John asks.

[Whatever you like,] the man says.

[I have been selling this soil for twenty years, and I have never had any disputes over money!] …

I see the hand offering another paper packet, a sparkling diamond shining on one of the fingers. Could this sparkling thing be the price of twenty years? John casually takes out a whole sum of money from his pocket, trading for two thin white paper packets. The hand with the diamond then disappears. [Profiteering!] I sigh softly.

[No,] the other party objects, [This soil is useful. When I was little, going to school in the county, my mother would always give me a packet of soil every time I came back, saying lovingly, [If you get sick, add some white sugar and drink it with water!] One year I fell ill in the provincial capital, and my father specially brought me some soil to see me. Now, if my mother were still alive, she wouldn't forget to prepare it for me. My mother is gone, but I will never forget…]

He says softly, trickling like a fine, flowing spring. I can only listen.

The thick fog has not yet dissipated, and the sky and water remain connected in the vastness. We boarded the big ship together. Under the lights, I see that the young man's eyelids are a little red. Because the fog is too thick, the ship doesn't seem to be leaving for the time being. We see emotions of parting rolling everywhere, electric-like, a knowing ache. We become even more silent.

Seeing this situation, I can't help but think—

This is the tangible and intangible heat of native soil! Our overseas Chinese, no matter where they go, are always thinking of their native soil! Especially at this time, at this time, people will remember their native soil even more.

I point to John. Look, the soil merchant with the diamond on his finger has appeared on the big ship again.

Strolling 193

— TK

Tomorrow (6) 194

— (By Joseph Conrad) Translated by Wu Xiangyu

She obeyed him silently, listening patiently beside the wooden fence; her eyes looking downwards, working on her knitting. Redness appeared very slowly on the pale skin under her rather untidy, abundant red hair. Her father's hair was conspicuously red.

She had a plump figure; a tired, weary face. When Captain Hagberd boasted about the necessity and appropriateness of family, and the joys of the hearth, she only wore a slight smile on her lips. The happiness of her family, in the best ten years of her life, was limited to taking care of her father.

Crude shouts from the upstairs window often interrupted their conversation. She would immediately and leisurely put away her knitting or sewing. Meanwhile, this angry roar calling her name, continuing, would make the fishermen wandering on the seawall across the road turn their heads towards these two cottages. She would often slowly walk in through the front door, and after a moment, everything would be silent. Soon after, she would come out again, supporting a crude, unreasonable, bad-tempered, melancholic-faced man who looked like a hippopotamus.

He was a widowed shipbuilder, who had suddenly gone blind many years ago when his business was flourishing. He usually treated his daughter as if she were responsible for his incurable disease. People always heard him shouting hoarsely, as if cursing heaven, a situation he never noticed himself: he had enough money to provide him with ham and eggs every day. For this, he often thanked God in a boisterous voice, just as he cursed.

Captain Hagberd had a very bad impression of his tenant, and he even once said to Miss Bessant, [He's a real excessive fellow, my dear.]

That day, she was making a woolen livelihood, knitting a pair of socks for her father, who always hoped she could dutifully provide for his needs, but he hated woolen work. At that time, when she was knitting the heel, his eyes had to be fixed on the needles.

[Of course, this is not like having a son to plan for him,] Captain Hagberd went on vaguely. Girls, of course, don't need that much—hum—hum. They don't leave home, my dear.]

[Not necessarily,] Miss Bessant said quietly.

Captain Hagberd laughed knowingly amidst the upturned clods of earth. From his sailor's outfit, his weather-beaten face, and his beard like old Father Neptune, he looked like a deposed sea god, only his trident had been replaced with a shovel.

Talking Points

Society with a Monkish Mentality 195

— Pi

Yesterday, I saw in the newspaper that Yang Huazhao had become a monk in Mount Putuo's Luojia Mountain for three years, and Liu Yuchun is also a monk in Putuo's Jiulong Peng. However, although Yang and Liu have become monks in Putuo, their whereabouts are very secret, so no one recognizes them as survivors of military life.

Yang Huazhao was a famous general during the Qi-Lu War in 1924. Liu Yuchun was a valiant general who stubbornly resisted the Revolutionary Army while defending Wuchang in 1926. Now, Yang has become a monk in Putuo's Luojia Mountain, and Liu is a monk in Putuo's Jiulong Peng. These two were once demonic figures who killed without batting an eye. Now, they have both entered the empty gate of Buddhism, truly [laying down the butcher's knife and becoming a Buddha on the spot]. One cannot but say that these two heroes have awakened.

Let's set aside the merits and demerits of Yang and Liu in the past for now. But after all, these two are both capable and experienced warriors. In today's world of iron and blood, there is a great need for this kind of talent to defend the country and promote national spirit. Therefore, having two more monks in Mount Putuo is a direct loss to individuals and an indirect loss to the nation.

Becoming a monk is originally the last resort of a hero, and a hero is originally the incarnation of a monk. If there is a way out, one becomes a hero; if there is no way out, one becomes a monk. Looking at it historically, it is originally a very common thing. Becoming a monk is originally a way of passive living, but heroes are like this, and non-heroes are also like this. Although there are still few visible monks in society now, there are actually many invisible monks, because the mentality of society now is a monkish mentality.

For example, [suicide] is a monkish mentality, [indulging in wine and women] is also a monkish mentality. Handling affairs with [the mentality of holding a post for only five days] is a monkish mentality. [Enjoying today's wine today] is also a monkish mentality. Meeting a friend and always asking [How have you been passing the time lately?] is a monkish mentality. [Being a human being is really very boring] is also a monkish mentality. When this kind of thinking spreads, it becomes a passive society, a passive nation. If individuals are passive, then individuals have no hope. If society is passive, then society has no hope. If the nation is passive, then the nation has no hope.

The cultivation of a passive mentality in the people is nothing more than two paths: (1) being invaded by imperialists, making it impossible to turn over for a while; (2) having no way out due to the poor social and economic system. The so-called [not knowing what will happen tomorrow] and [not planning for a human life in the next life]. The cultivation of such a mentality is really the fundamental element of social depravity. [There is no greater sorrow than the death of the heart], which is the most incurable thing.

I am not issuing this kind of argument because I feel sorry for Yang and Liu becoming monks. It is because Yang and Liu becoming monks made me feel that the passive state of society now is the same as the passive concepts of Yang and Liu in many ways, so I can't help but feel chills. As Yao Guangxiao's sister said to Guangxiao, [I have never seen a good person who couldn't become a monk.] Then Yang and Liu being able to become monks is still good. There are many friends who can't become monks but are still secular, who are even worse than monks.

Winter in the Capital 196

— Ran

Winter has driven the noble ladies from the bustling Zhuque Road back to their lonely boudoirs.

What's left are only the emaciated beggars. Hunger and cold, batch after batch, driven by the increasing speed of time, drive them out of their homes, out of the fields, wandering to the streets, wandering to the capital, usurping the red and green positions of the ladies, adorning the desolation of Zhuque Road.

Winter on Zhuque Road is an abandoned mistress; a patient with third-stage syphilis.

The 30th of May Park, First Park, Qinhuai River, Yuhuatai... These many scenic spots that once stirred the emotions of thousands of men and women, now, except for weekends, only occasionally have a few young students and a few couples, and no longer attract people's footprints.

Falling maple leaves, broken stems and residual branches are great poetic material for poets. But we only hear intermittent hibernating insects, playing the elegy of autumn mournfully among the withered branches and weeds.

National, Capital, Nanjing... These several cinemas, however, with the arrival of winter, have become particularly prosperous. The ladies and gentlemen, not born with bones that can endure the cold, dare not show their faces in the northwest wind, locked in their boudoirs all day, too bored, the most appropriate place to go is to the cinema. There, there are hot water radiators, the warm spring weather, spring seats, cracking a few pine nuts, talking about Elizabeth and Joan Blondell for a while, and a cold winter night will pass warmly. Moreover, the words romantic, mysterious, and exotic are flashing with bright eyes, staring at them, right?

Walking in here, the bosses can also give you a guaranteed satisfaction ticket! Because he can comply with

Page 22

the [audience's]? demands, and even use the scissors himself to cut the film again after the film censorship committee has cut it once. In this way, he guarantees that you will never be disappointed!

Finally, the dark mouth of the demon opens wide, and people are thrown out like goods in a warehouse. Women lean softly like lazy cats on the shoulders of men, twisting their willow waists, get into a 1935 Chevrolet, and leave with a "wobble wobble." The smell of gasoline mixed with the smell of soil pounces on the noses of passers-by. How many people are stunned, dreaming the dream of the great Han Emperor Liu Bang--[Can I take his place?]

One thing is too anticlimactic, the capital city is so big, but there is not a single dance hall. The young masters who have gone abroad and drunk seawater are cursing all day long: [Nanjing, a winter in the desert!] The cinema films are too bad, the courtesans' performances in Confucius Temple are also not popular, and the Great World Amusement Park is even worse. Only: [Let's go to Shanghai!] So, on Saturday afternoons, the business of the first- and second-class Jinghu trains is especially good.

The [venerable gentlemen], whose beards are not even a handful long, wear a black coat, get on their private cars, clang, clang, pull up to the Confucius Temple, where there is a row of more than twenty teahouses facing south, such as Kuiguang Pavilion, Qifang Building, etc. Brew a pot of rain before the season, eat a few vegetable buns, bask in the warm sunlight, talk about a few anecdotes of the Six Dynasties, flip through the newly released opera newspaper, or play a game or two of Go. The biting winter wind doesn't bother them and quietly subsides.

The ban on prostitution is strict, and the lives of the small clerks are very dull. Go to Linfeng Pavilion and Xueyuan in Confucius Temple to listen to the courtesans sing, [Eyes on, hands off,] too boring, and even flying paper cages is now prohibited. Then, pick a colleague's house, call a [lover] over, sit on a stool, warm a stove, play thirty-six rounds of mahjong, and the winter night will not pass well? Fortunately, if you don't make a noise in your own home, the police will never come to bother you. Who doesn't know that even though these are just small clerks, who doesn't have a strong background?

But it's just hard for the shop assistants who make a living from business. When the northwest wind comes, it seems to blow away a lot of their business. From early morning, they are cold and until the evening. Most of the store equipment is still old-fashioned. The old northwest wind blows into the counter where the shop assistants are every day and night. Finally, they endure until the vertical door is closed, and take the day's bad luck to the Great World. Two cents for a small ocean ticket, buy one get one free, hook up with a [white silk], and make a riot for a while. Open a room? The winter check is tight, and couples are caught in the substation from time to time. It's a small matter to pay a few dollars in fines, but a night in [winter prison] is really hard to bear.

However, the most bitter is still their boss. Hanging a sign and propping up a storefront, it is not as good as in previous years. The recession makes them look worried and burdened with a lot of debt. How will they spend the New Year?

In winter in the capital, some people are hiding in greenhouses, and more people are wandering on the streets. Some are laughing happily, but more are sobbing secretly!

The Sorrow of Life 197

— Jiang Zuo

Call Me Uncle 198

— Nan Yan

When I returned to my residence from the restaurant, the amah handed me a letter. She said it was sent by a villager and that he would be coming again later. I opened the letter, and it was written like this:

[Friend, if there is still a shadow of your friend from a few years ago lingering in your mind, and you would like to meet, then please come with the person delivering the letter.]

Such simple words, and without a signature, the mystery is really perplexing. I repeatedly identified the structure and brushstrokes of almost every word, examining them very carefully, but in the end, I was still at a loss.

After a while, the messenger arrived. So I asked him:

[Who told you to deliver this?]

[The young master told me to deliver it.]

[What is the young master's surname?]

[I don't know.]

So, I pondered for a while, and finally decided to go there.

On the road leading to Village B, I walked silently, trying my best to find clues. From the sentence structure, I determined that it came from Old Chen's handwriting, but immediately felt that it was not very accurate. In any case, Old Chen would never run to the countryside, and besides, the brushstrokes were so naive.

[Then who is it?] I asked myself secretly.

The villager walking in front, he turned his head from time to time to look at me. Perhaps he felt too strange, why was the guest behind him always looking at the ground?

Arriving at Village B, we also curved and turned through a few small alleys. Finally, next to an old house, on a newly built small building, from afar, I saw a woman leaning against the railing, looking towards me, and waving her hand incessantly. I also looked at her suspiciously.

Slowly approaching the small building, people were naturally seen very clearly, I nodded to her in surprise. I really didn't dream that I would meet her here, whom I hadn't seen for a long time, the person I once loved!

[Come in.] She smiled, then turned around and said loudly:

[The guest has arrived.]

I embraced a full heart of excitement, mixed with the aftertaste of that tragic parting at the time, and walked inside.

The stairs clattered noisily. She came down, followed by a strange man, holding a cute little child in his arms.

[I really didn't dream that we would have this meeting today,] she smiled slightly, then pointed to the stranger and said:

[This is my husband.] Then, from her husband's hands, she took the child and taught him to call me [Uncle.] The child shyly hid in her arms.

I watched silently without a word, what else could I say!

The Pleasure of Buying Old Books 199

— Overseas Student

The habit of buying books is good. However, sometimes it is not good; and some people are also not good. For example, when you are very poor, and even the problem of eating is difficult to solve, one day you pass a bookstore and see a newly printed book; and this new book happens to be the one you love to read, so you buy it with all you have. In this way, although you have the book, what about when your stomach gets hungry? Some people, in fact, their monthly income can only cover household expenses, and there is absolutely no extra money to buy books, but they still insist on going to bookstores, making their lives a problem; these examples all show that buying books is indeed a virtue, but it is not something everyone can do.

I am a person who likes to buy books. However, I am also distressed by not having so much money. The other day, I saw a new book, Soviet Literature, which had arrived at the Commercial Press. The content was very rich. I flipped through it for a long time, but because it was worth two and a half US dollars, I dared not buy it, and I really couldn't afford it. Chinese books, on the other hand, are much cheaper. For example, a translation of Ellis's [Shaw's Biography] only sells for two dollars. You can't say it's not cheap. Who knew that I didn't even have two dollars that day. So, in the end, I had to come out empty-handed!

However, books still have to be read after all. So I thought of the way to buy old books.

In fact, as recently as when the bookstores on Fourth Avenue were selling cheap books, it was very worthwhile to go and find a few books. Because, although the books had been out for a while, the copies were not very damaged; and the prices were all below half price. At that time, I spent half a day looking for many books that I wanted to buy but couldn't afford before. Taking the recent example, I bought Wilde's [The Picture of Dorian Gray] in a bookstore for nine cents; this is a famous aesthetic work that I have long wanted to see. The joy of taking this book back and reading it under the lamp is indescribable. There are many people in the world who love to read, and I hope they can all buy their favorite books.

Storytelling Singing 201

Yao Xiao'an's Pearl Pagoda

Zhongxi (1040) 10:00 AM to 11:00 AM

Opening [Prostitute's Lament]

The fourth month is clear and the rain is just clearing. The doors are deserted and I am heartbroken. Since ancient times, the world has been cold and warm. The life of a prostitute is only new for a short time. Before puberty, I touch people's hearts. Touching hands and feet and kissing. Fifteen or sixteen is when the flower first blooms. It's like the moon is especially bright in the middle of autumn. Seventeen and eighteen are loved by everyone. The lotus coming out of the water is fragrant and new. At the age of twenty, it is the willow in the third month of spring. The orioles keep weaving past the sparrows. There are many rich cars and horses in front of the door. The madam is like a treasure in the palm. It is clear and bright day and night. Playful young men come like clouds. A young master is just getting on his horse outside the door. And it is reported that the young master is coming early. Being close and loving each other, there is no end to how much false warmth. Now the flowers are withered and the moon has set. It's not as touching as it used to be. There are only desolate cars and horses in front of the door. The pearl in the palm has turned into dust. There is no one on the Cold Food Festival. The playful young men are nowhere to be seen. Where have the sad young men gone? The翩翩公子 is not coming. Who will love him? What false warmth is there? I feel so sad.

Wu Er's head is filled with heart. He hurriedly carried the bones back home. He prepared some yellow paper and ingots. Kneeling down in front of the spirit, he called out to his brother. You died unclearly. If someone harms you. I hope my brother will entrust me with a dream at midnight. Leaning on the mourning altar, he suddenly fell asleep.
